United States Pursuing International Monetary Agreement, Minting Silver Coins Based on Silver-Gold Ratio 29

(Washington) Political and diplomatic circles predict that the United States and other countries are about to conclude an international agreement in order to mint silver coins in accordance with a unified gold-silver ratio among the countries. Regarding this matter, talks have been held among the countries in recent days, and an international conference will be proposed for discussion after considerable results have been achieved. Well-informed sources believe that President Roosevelt deeply wishes to avoid being forced to pass legislation on silver during the current congressional session. The aforementioned international talks are related to the President's wishes. It is generally explained that if the various bills for minting silver coins currently submitted to Congress are passed, there will be no possibility of establishing any international agreements on silver. According to reports, the US government recently sent two currency experts, Roasborth and Tang, to China and Japan to investigate. One of them was tasked with estimating the amount of silver stored in the Far East. In addition, the US government sent financial observers to other countries. President Roosevelt originally scheduled a meeting with Senator King, a representative of the silver group, for today. This meeting has now been postponed to next Monday. Thomas, one of the leaders of the Senate silver group (who recently proposed nationalizing silver in the Senate), also declared that members of Congress related to monetary issues, especially silver issues, will soon convene a meeting. Currency experts, such as Professor Warren, the founder of the "dollar commodity" theory, believe that the combination of silver and the world's monetary system would stabilize world prices, and after silver is minted into world currency, the total amount of world currency will increase, and the basis for international trade will also increase in the same proportion. However, it is still difficult to determine which countries can join this international agreement because no one knows the current global silver reserves. According to Professor Warren's estimates, the amount of silver minted into currency in the hundred years from 1813 to 1930 should reach 30,191,750 tons. (Havas, 20th)

The World is Shrouded in War Clouds: Armament Factories in Various Countries are Rushing to Produce Munitions, British Insurers Dare Not Underwrite War Insurance, Some Speculate That a European War Will Break Out Again Within Two Years 30

(New York) Here, speculation on a European war is underway. The ratio of those who do not believe that a war will occur in Europe in the next twelve months is 107 to 1. However, the ratio of those who predict that a war will occur within two years is 140 to 1. War insurance underwriters in London dare not underwrite war insurance for five years, even if they get extremely high premiums. The terror of war has made insurers feel highly threatened. This is really caused by the stimulation of military activities. The manufacturing of armaments in various countries is becoming increasingly strained. In the Creusot area in the wine-producing regions of southern France, the sky is now shrouded in smoke. The Skoda factory in Czechoslovakia, the Vickers-Armstrongs plant in the United Kingdom, the Mitsui plant in Japan, and other armament manufacturing plants are all in a state of chained tension. From Washington to Tokyo, there are alert armament managers selling munitions. The United States has declared that it will build a navy for defensive purposes in order to uphold the dignity of treaties. Therefore, Britain and Japan also intend to start building new ships, using the excuse that the current treaty ratio is insufficient to cope with the current situation. Saltpeter is the raw material for explosives. This type of munition raw material has been transported through the Panama Canal and the Suez Canal. The United States has sold 25,000 tons to France. Currently, the US senators have already noticed the competition of US armament manufacturers to sell munitions and will begin an investigation into the current state of the US armament industry, advocating that the government immediately take over all armament raw material manufacturing industries. However, this investigation is very difficult and involves every citizen. For example, a farmer producing one acre of cotton, the cotton is a raw material for munitions. As for manufacturing a car or an airplane, no matter how meager its materials are, it can all be transformed into munitions. Therefore, the main raw materials for munitions are also the materials for creating civilization, and it is difficult to distinguish between them. (National Telegram, 19th)

Britain Planning to Shorten Air Mail to the Far East 37

(London) According to the Daily Telegraph, Britain, Canada, and Newfoundland have now concluded a postal agreement, which will be implemented this summer. At that time, a very fast delivery method for mail to the Far East will be available, shortening the journey from London to Montreal, Canada, from six and a half days to four days. Furthermore, the method of connecting Canadian and American trains and airlines can be used to make postal delivery in North America even faster. When Canadian Pacific Railway Company ships arrive west of Ireland, airplanes can catch up and transmit mail. When the ship arrives at the St. Lawrence, airplanes can wait there to receive mail. The Canadian airplanes can take off in the summer from Belle Isle, 500 miles to Shediac in New Brunswick, and in the winter, when the mouth of the St. Lawrence River is frozen, the airplanes can take off 550 miles from Cape Race to Shediac. The east-bound aircraft will also follow this method. The Canadian airline is not yet completed, so at present, the mail can only be flown to Rimouski and then transported by rail. As for the mail passing through the Pacific, it still needs to be transported by ship, but the time from Britain to the Far East will be greatly shortened. (Reuters Communication, March 17)

The Stalemate Between France and Germany: The Disarmament Conference Only Has a Glimmer of Hope, America Cannot Stand Idly By, and is Preparing to Participate in General Discussions. Britain and the United States Will Unite to Formulate a New Plan. 41

(London) Politicians throughout Europe are deeply disturbed by the breakdown of disarmament negotiations over the past six months and the stalemate in the hostile actions of France and Germany. Germany explicitly demands the right to rearm, while France accuses it of violating the peace treaty and demands that other countries guarantee French security as a prerequisite for acknowledging Germany's military increase. German semi-official sources vehemently deny accusations that Germany's rearmament violates the Treaty of Versailles. However, British politicians have not given up hope and believe that the General Disarmament Commission to be held in Geneva on May 23rd may still achieve some success. Politicians generally believe that if European countries fail to resolve these disputes, an unprecedented arms race will begin. This is why politicians cannot bear to see the Disarmament Conference die. The failure of the Disarmament Conference is tantamount to pronouncing the death sentence of the League of Nations. (League of Nations Telegram, 20th)

(Washington) Today, the State Department stated that the United States is prepared to return to Geneva to resume disarmament discussions. This is the only statement made by Washington authorities since the French diplomatic note was published. (Reuters Telegram, 19th)

(New York) The New York Times' Washington correspondent predicted today that the United States, Britain, and former neutral countries will form a disarmament bloc as a result of the position taken by France. This bloc will formulate a new plan to be submitted to the General Disarmament Commission, which will reconvene on May 23rd. (Reuters Telegram, 20th)

(Washington) President Roosevelt has anticipated the collapse of the Disarmament Conference. The government has not changed the policy announced to Congress on January 3rd this year. At that time, the President stated that the United States could not participate in European political issues but was willing to cooperate with European countries to complete any plan to reduce armaments and commercial obstacles. The State Department is quite concerned about the collapse of disarmament negotiations but does not express surprise. French Ambassador to the United States Paul Claudel delivered a copy of the French note to Britain to Undersecretary of State Philip. State Department officials immediately studied it. According to most officials, the French note tends to hand over the disarmament issue to the General Disarmament Commission to be held in Geneva on May 23rd and hopes that Davis can participate in the meeting as an informal representative of the United States. Although government leaders have informally stated that any rearmament goes against the purpose of the Disarmament Conference, the United States has never definitively expressed its position on Germany's demand for equality in armaments. According to most officials, European countries have been negotiating for two years, but no compromise has yet been reached on the basic principles of the disarmament convention. Instead, global military spending exceeds US$5,000,000,000 per year. In substance, the 1934 military budgets of various countries are also higher than when the Disarmament Conference opened in 1932. The United States has always maintained an observer attitude towards the Disarmament Conference, but the United States often has informal representatives participating to support various actions. (National Telegram, 19th)

Draft of the New Austrian Constitution: Leaning Towards Fascism, a Precursor to the Restoration of the Empire 46

The Vienna Official Gazette announced today that the new constitution has been completed. Austria's inclination towards fascism is becoming increasingly apparent. The Austrian Cabinet will meet at the end of this week to decide on the date of the promulgation of the constitution and will try to promote Archduke Otto of the Habsburg royal family to return to Austria as regent or even as the monarch of Austria. Premier Dollfuss suggested today that in order to turn the nascent republic into a fascist state, he will resign from his position as a foundation for government reorganization. A transitional constitutional rule was implemented last month as a preparation. According to Dollfuss's concept of a fascist corporate state, Austria will be reorganized by incorporating Italian fascism, German socialism, Soviet communism, syndical socialism, medieval feudalism, and Catholicism. Most European diplomats and political observers expect Austria to return to the rule of the Habsburg royal family and become a monarchy. According to observers, the construction of a fascist state is only a precursor to the construction of a monarchical state. Premier Dollfuss was born into a farming family and is a devout Catholic. He has always believed in the imperial system. The imperial system that once ruled Austria was the strongest empire in the world and the most powerful supporter of the church. Dollfuss is by nature opposed to Marxist socialism and is deeply skeptical of the so-called mechanized 20th century and the industrial revolution. After the Great War, the Austrian imperial system disintegrated, and socialism took the opportunity to rise and rule Austria for a long time until the situation began to change two years ago. At that time, Austria's economic, financial, and cultural conditions were deteriorating, and the political situation was also precarious, but there were no obvious signs on the surface. Now Premier Dollfuss plans to build a new social system to replace the parliamentary system according to the new constitution he announced yesterday. (National Telegram, 20th)

(Rome) Prince Starhemberg, leader of the Austrian Patriotic League, focused on internal Austrian issues in his political talks here, especially with Prime Minister Mussolini. Starhemberg specifically explained how the Austrian constitution is evolving, saying that Parliament will be convened in early May, but in a reduced form and with a fixed term. Within this term, Parliament's task is to prepare for constitutional amendments. Austrian government personnel will be greatly adjusted, and Prince Starhemberg will be the Deputy Prime Minister. We still remember that when Vienna was in chaos and the Austrian government punished the Socialist Party, Italian newspapers praised Dollfuss and Prince Starhemberg equally. Since then, Italian newspapers have said that Dollfuss should take the opportunity to amend the constitution so that Austria is closer to Pan-Germanism. At that time, it was generally advocated that Prince Starhemberg should cooperate closely with the Austrian government. The situation was like this on that day, so the reason why Prince Starhemberg came to Rome on the eve of the constitutional amendment to contact all parties can be imagined. It is widely rumored that when Prince Starhemberg arrived here, German Deputy Prime Minister Papen was about to leave Rome to return to his country, and the two had met. It is also said that Prince Starhemberg came this time to consult with Italy on the purchase of military equipment. Various rumors have been clearly denied. (Jinan) Bandit Liu sneaked southwest from Shichang, Juxian this morning. At 9:00, he reached Yangjia Guanzhuang in Rizhao territory and was intercepted by Zhan Shutang, commander of the Eighty-first Division, who killed more than 30 bandits, captured more than 40, seized 18 horses, more than 20 guns, and more than 70 bullets. The bandits collapsed and fled wildly in all directions. At 3:00 pm, they fled northwest from Hezhuang, about 50 miles southwest of Rizhao, to Shengong Mountain, where they were intercepted by Zhan Shutang again, killing more than 20. The bandits fled southeast to Zhu Cao, no more than four or five miles from Ganyu County in Jiangsu. Han Lingzhan Shutang led the division's directly subordinate battalion companies and Tang Bangzhi's brigade Zhang Derun's regiment to pursue them. Gu Liangmin, commander of the Twenty-second Division, led his directly subordinate troops east from Linyi to intercept them. The remaining troops all returned to their original defenses. In total, this suppression of Liu resulted in the seizure of more than 400 rifles, more than 20 machine guns, more than 10 mortars, and more than 40 horses. The number of people and horses killed is uncertain. More than 290 bandits were captured in Anqiu. Han ordered the county magistrate to interrogate them. Those under the age of 15 and over the age of 50 were spared death and escorted to Jinan for disposal. The remaining more than 150 people have been executed by shooting in Anqiu. Cheng Shijinbiao, a 17-year-old lieutenant adjutant in Tang's brigade, killed 24 bandits and seized 15 guns while suppressing bandits in Qishan, Anqiu. The headquarters issued an order to commend him. (Special Telegram, 19th)

(Hangzhou) The Panchen Lama is scheduled to come to Hangzhou on the 24th. Jiang donated 5,000 yuan and telegraphed Zhou Junyan to send it on his behalf. Liu Xiang donated 1,000 yuan. The Zhejiang Branch of the Cultural Society believes that saving the crisis and seeking survival can only be achieved by promoting national consciousness and building the national economy, not by chanting scriptures, holding religious ceremonies, and worshipping gods and Buddhas. It issued a declaration opposing the Kalachakra Dharma Assembly. (Special Telegram, 20th)

Railway Construction Bond Regulations 60

(Nanjing) Regulations for the First Issue of Railway Construction Bonds of the Republic of China, 1934. Article 1: In order to realize the plan of building new railways and consolidating old railways, the Ministry of Railways will issue the first issue of public bonds of 12 million yuan, specifically for the Yupi Railway, named the First Issue of Railway Construction Bonds of the Republic of China, 1934. Article 2: These public bonds will be issued on May 1, 1934. Article 3: These public bonds will be issued at 98% of the face value. Article 4: The annual interest rate of these public bonds is set at 6%, calculated based on the face value, starting from the date of issuance, and interest will be paid twice a year on June 30 and December 31. Article 5: These public bonds will only pay interest for the first two periods. Starting from June 30, 1935, the principal will be repaid using a lottery method in accordance with the amount specified in the principal and interest repayment schedule, in 16 installments over eight years, until December 31, 1942, when all the principal will be fully repaid. The aforementioned lottery will be held 20 days before each principal repayment period. Article 6: The repayment of principal and interest of these public bonds will be handled by the Public Bond Fund Management Committee entrusted by the Ministry of Railways as mentioned in Article 8, and the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications will be designated as the agencies for paying principal and interest. Article 7: The repayment of principal and interest of these public bonds will be funded by the surplus profits of the state-owned railways directly under the Ministry of Railways. The Ministry of Railways will submit the amount listed in the principal and interest repayment schedule to the bank designated by the Fund Management Committee for special storage each month in order to prepare for payment upon maturity. Article 8: The Public Bond Fund will be composed of three representatives from the Ministry of Railways, one representative each from the Ministry of Finance and the Auditing Department, and two representatives publicly elected by the issuing banks to jointly form the Public Bond Fund Management Committee, which will be responsible for safekeeping. The organizational regulations will be drafted by the Ministry of Railways and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. Article 9: These public bonds will be used exclusively for the purposes specified in Article 1 and may not be used for other purposes. Article 10: The face value of these public bonds is set at 1,000 yuan, 500 yuan, and 100 yuan. Article 11: These public bonds are in bearer form and may be freely bought, sold, and mortgaged. Article 12: Those who forge these public bonds or engage in acts of damaging credit will be punished by the judicial authorities according to law. Article 13: These regulations will be implemented from the date of promulgation. (Central News Agency Telegram, 20th)

Jin Shuren Case Adjourned for Continued Hearing 62

(Nanjing) The case of former Xinjiang Chairman Jin Shuren was continued at 1:00 PM on the 20th by Lu Wenlan, the presiding judge of the Jiangsu Higher and other courts. Jin Shuren stated that due to illness, three witnesses—Wu Aichen, Xinjiang's special envoy for foreign affairs, and Gong Bicheng and others, representatives of the Xinjiang Provincial Government—did not appear in court, making deliberation impossible. Lu Wenlan immediately announced a postponement. (20th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Jin Shuren case was continued at the Jiangning District Court at 1:00 PM on the 20th. Presiding judge Lu Wenlan, judge Fang Wensiwen, defense lawyers Zhang Shaozeng and Wang Ruilin, and accuser Aisa, among others, entered the court. The presiding judge announced the opening of the court, stating that Jin was ill and the hearing was postponed. Witnesses Wu Aichen had gone to Jiangxi, and Gong Bicheng had left Beijing, making it impossible to proceed. The trial was suspended according to law and the hearing was rescheduled. Subsequently, the defense lawyers requested the cessation of the defendant's secret detention to allow him to move to a hospital, citing the Jiangsu High Court's ruling on April 9, which rejected the cessation of secret detention. An appeal was filed on the 16th. The presiding judge agreed to handle it according to the appeal procedure. The court adjourned at 2:00 PM. Lu will return to Jiangsu in two or three days, and the continued hearing will be postponed. (20th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) A measles epidemic is spreading in the city. Many people have contracted the disease and died since the beginning of spring. Ministry of Communications Issues Order Banning Fare Reductions and Free Passage on Ships 65

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Communications submitted a report to the Executive Yuan, issuing an order to its subordinates to prohibit fare reductions and free passage on ships. The report stated that the domestic shipping industry has not yet developed and has been in a recession for years, impacting the economy. Recently, cases of military and political personnel forcibly demanding fare reductions and free passage have emerged endlessly, causing significant losses to shipping merchants. The report requested that a nationwide order be issued to all military and political agencies, instructing them not to force fare reductions or free passenger transport in the future to alleviate the difficulties of shipping. (20th Special Dispatch)

Chen Taosheng, a technician from the Ministry of Industry, and Zhou Dagu, a chemist from the Ministry of Finance, will go to Qiongya and Lianzhou to conduct on-site investigations. Drastic Increase in Japanese and Korean Population Along the South Manchuria Railway Line 103

Last Year's Statistics Exceeded 40,000

Harbin Increases by 500 Every Month

A dispatch from Changchun states that since the September 18th Incident, the number of Japanese coming to our Northeast has been quite astonishing, and the Korean population has also increased significantly. There is also a small number of Taiwanese. The Japanese all reside in major cities along the South Manchuria Railway line, especially Changchun, which has the most. According to a recent survey by the police station of the Japanese Consulate General in Harbin, the number of Japanese in the city has tripled since before the September 18th Incident, now totaling 10,500, with an average monthly increase of 500. This is only for Harbin, and the number in other places is even greater. The following is a record of the statistics on the Japanese, Korean, and Taiwanese population in the cities along the South Manchuria Railway line (not including all of the Northeast) surveyed by the consulate police station and the puppet police station in November of last year (the numbers have increased even more this year, and no statistics are available yet).

Changchun 104

According to a survey by the Changchun Police Station, (1) Japanese: 11,965 men, with 7,525 employed and 4,440 dependents; 8,145 women, with 1,951 employed and 6,194 dependents, totaling 20,100 people. (2) Koreans: 1,293 men and 980 women, totaling 2,273 people. (3) Taiwanese: 14 men and 2 women, totaling 16 people. The total is 22,389 people, an increase of 5,995 compared to October of the previous year, with 4,807 households. According to statistics from the Changchun Consulate General Police Station, (1) Japanese: 2,615 men, with 1,962 employed and 653 dependents; 1,665 women, with 416 employed and 1,249 dependents, totaling 4,810 people. (2) Koreans: 3,390 men and 2,245 women, totaling 5,625 people. (3) Taiwanese: None. The total is 9,905 people, an increase of 4,282 compared to October of last year, with 1,534 households.

Fanjatun 105

According to statistics from the Fanjatun Police Station, (1) Japanese: 373 men, with 232 employed and 141 dependents; 229 women, with 7 employed and 299 dependents, totaling 673 people. (2) Koreans: 17 men and 18 women, totaling 35 people. (3) Taiwanese: None. The total is 770 people, an increase of 99 compared to October of last year, with 140 households.

Gongzhuling 106

According to a survey by the Gongzhuling Police Station, (1) Japanese: 1,436 men, with 778 employed and 658 dependents; 1,241 women, with 131 employed and 1,110 dependents, totaling 2,677 people. (2) Koreans: 169 men and 718 women, totaling 347 people. (3) Taiwanese: None. The total is 3,024 people, an increase of 124 compared to October of last year, with 728 households.

Sipingjie 107

According to statistics from the Sipingjie Police Station, (1) Japanese: 2,651 men, with 1,615 employed and 1,036 dependents; 2,327 women, with 320 employed and 2,007 dependents, totaling 4,178 people. (2) Koreans: 474 men and 459 women, totaling 933 people. (3) Taiwanese: The total is 5,911 people, an increase of 590 compared to October of last year, with 1,243 households.

Nong'an 108

According to a survey by the Nong'an Japanese Consulate Branch Police Station, (1) Japanese: 22 men, all employed, no dependents; 1 woman, unemployed, 1 dependent, totaling 23 people. (2) Koreans: 189 men and 171 women, totaling 360 people. (3) Taiwanese: None. The total is 383 people, a decrease of 1 compared to October of last year, with 25 households.

The total Japanese and Korean population: (1) Japanese: 32,740 people, 19,062 men, with 12,134 employed and 6,928 dependents; 13,678 women, with 2,825 employed and 6,928 dependents. (2) Koreans: 9,573 people, 5,522 men. (3) Taiwanese: 16 people, 14 men and 2 women. (Northeast News Agency)

International Commercial Telegram 109

Reuters Special Business Telegram, April 20th

Gold and Silver 110

London Gold Price: Today's London gold price is 135 shillings and 2.5 pence, a decrease of 0.5 pence compared to yesterday.

London Silver: This morning, the London silver market saw little trading. India made purchases, but otherwise, it was quiet. The spot price is listed at 19.875 pence, the same as yesterday. The futures price increased by 0.0625 to 20 pence. New York Silver: News from Washington about the international agreement to reuse silver coins and rumors that President Roosevelt might approve revised silver proposals are maintaining today's silver market. The silver market opened steadily, with prices 50 pounds sterling lower than London, but in a more stable position than a week ago. Bombay Silver: The Bombay silver market closed steadily, with the spot price at 54 rupees and 14 annas, an increase of 2 annas. Futures also increased by 2 annas.

Exchange Rates 111

British and American Exchange: The London foreign exchange market was quiet today. The opening British-American exchange rate was 5 dollars, 1 dime, 4 cents, and 75 mils, an increase of 125 mils compared to yesterday's closing price. It gradually increased to 5 dollars, 1 dime, 5 cents, and 3125 mils by late morning, but then decreased by 125 mils. The most recent price is 5 dollars, 1 dime, 5 cents, and 1875 mils.

British and French: The opening was 77 francs 75, a decrease of 3 pounds sterling compared to yesterday's closing. It then increased by 5 pounds sterling, but by 2 PM, it had fallen to 77 francs 71, 4 pounds sterling lower than the opening.

American-British: The opening exchange rate for American-British was 5.15.00 today. The second transaction was the same price. The third transaction was 5.15.75. The fourth and fifth transactions were the same as the previous transaction. The sixth transaction was 5.16.00.

American-French: The opening exchange rate for American-French today was 6.63.3115.

Cotton and Wheat 112

American Cotton: Cotton brokers have a more pleasant interest today, but the market price fell at the opening due to the closure of long positions and selling by the South and local sellers. Demand from domestic merchants, European merchants, and Liverpool is still strong, but cotton is still trending downward due to the continuous closure of long positions and the concern caused by news of silver expansion. The market situation is quiet when prices fall. Indian Cotton: The Bombay cotton market initially fell due to the closure of long positions and selling by retail investors and Japanese merchants, but rebounded slightly due to purchases by European exporters. The closing price for July-August white cotton was 195 rupees 75, a decrease of 2 rupees.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market is as loose as yesterday. Yesterday, the July price was 5.87 at 1:00 PM, a decrease of 4 pounds sterling.

British Wheat: Liverpool wheat for July delivery fell 0.25 to 4 shillings and 3.5 pence.

Rubber 113

London Rubber: The London rubber market is more stable today. At noon, the trading price for July and September delivery was 5 pence 875, an increase of 0.0625. New York Rubber: The rubber market is active, with prices rising due to news from London and Amsterdam that a restriction plan could be gradually adopted. Market sentiment is trending towards the long side, and traders are advocating purchases.

Securities 114

The New York stock market opened today with stability, and prices were slightly higher. This is because the market's recent performance can be seen as a sign of its strong underlying position. Furthermore, the weakness of the US dollar and sluggish commodity prices have led to renewed talk of inflation, which is another reason for the stock market's stable opening. However, a sense of anxiety still clearly exists, and market conditions are fluctuating and uncertain. Merchants are still being very cautious and waiting for developments. The volume of transactions in the first hour after the opening was 510,000 shares. The Jardine Matheson & Co. report on the prices of fifteen New York securities is listed below (as of 10:45 AM):

Inspection Report from the Northwest Our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya: Current Situation of Suiyuan Construction 116

At 3:00 AM on the 8th, we departed from Datong, still on the Xikai PingSui train. At daybreak, we arrived at Pingdiquan. Looking out the window, everything was white. I then realized that it had snowed heavily. The further west we went, the thicker the snow became. The snow-covered willows on both sides were especially crystal clear and dazzling, truly possessing the elegance of "Suddenly, like a spring breeze overnight, thousands and thousands of pear trees bloom." The land along the way was flat and wide, with the Sui River flowing smoothly. The water and grass were lush and beautiful, very suitable for cultivation and grazing. Occasionally, we saw smoke rising from what were mostly cave dwellings. The doors and walls were often painted with white circles or white tigers, which, I heard, were used to scare away wolves at night. In Fushengzhuang, there was a cave dwelling with walls made of cut earth. A passage through the middle served as the door. On the right was written "Eight-Strand Rope Shop," and on the left was written "Tea and Water Provided." Next to it was a drawing of a person carrying goods, with the words "Liu (likely a typo for "Stay") Person" written beside it. It was clear that this was a roadside inn. As for the shop's name, "Eight-Strand Rope," it was because the travelers passing by, whether they were using camels or porters, could not do without this item.

At first, we saw snow-covered willows, but gradually they disappeared. To the right of the road, the mountains were bare. Occasionally, we saw flocks of sheep, sometimes near, sometimes far, moving slowly. The earth houses in the rural villages had flat roofs, on which cow dung was piled up for fuel. In the Baitajing area, there was a sandy beach stretching as far as the eye could see, some of which seemed to have been reclaimed, while others were still barren. Along the PingSui railway line, the vacant land on both sides had been surveyed and marked by the government. Apart from the land that had already been leased for cultivation, there were still more than 3,200 mu available. Even with the lowest rent of five jiao per mu, no one came forward to lease it. The vast land and sparse population of the Northwest were already evident here.

At 1:00 PM, we got off the train in Guisui. The cold wind after the snow made my ears ache terribly. There were more than a dozen sedan chairs in front of the station. The horses were mostly fat and lovely. It is indeed true that Chahar and Suiyuan produce good horses. The city has two parts, the old and the new, about four or five li apart. Government offices are mostly in the new city, while commerce and industry are entirely in the old city. The "New City Road" we passed through was well-built and smooth, with trees lining the road reaching a height of thirty zhang, neatly arranged. In the summer, the shade must be lush and refreshing. The "September 18th Memorial Hall," currently under construction, is located right next to the road on the north side. Since I came to the north, I don't seem to have seen the words "September 18th" anywhere. Now, suddenly seeing it in the border region gave me quite a shock.

I visited Mr. Feng Xi, the Director of the Suiyuan Provincial Construction Department, who spoke to me about the construction work in Suiyuan Province, which is very important. The following is a summary of his remarks:

Suiyuan is a base for the construction of the Northwest. To develop the Northwest, one must start with Suiyuan. However, trying to do everything at once is not allowed by financial resources and time. It is better to start with transportation, roads, telecommunications, water conservancy, agriculture, animal husbandry, and afforestation, and then proceed gradually. Suiyuan Province is originally a culturally backward area. For all construction plans, the first thing to do is to make the people understand, then train and test them, and then put them into practice. In recent years, the benefits of the work have been as follows. Suiyuan has a lot of desert land, and transportation has always been difficult. Repairing roads is extremely important. The roads that have been completed are: Baotou to Wulahai, 700 li, with 42 bridges; Jining to Taolin, 120 li; Fengzhen to Xinghe, 100 li; Suiyuan to Bailingmiao, 340 li; Qingshuihe to Helin, 150 li; Tuoketuo to Guisui, 140 li; the Bawanghe Bridge; and the roads in Guibao, 30 li. The construction of Jiazi Bridge, Suiyuan Bridge, Public Security Bridge, Datong Bridge, etc., is also underway. All the roads are being expanded.

The counties with completed telephone lines are: Fengzhen, Xinghe, Liangcheng, Helin, Saxian, Tongqu, etc. The loop lines in places such as Guisui, Wuchuan, Guyang, Wuyuan, Anbei, Tuoketuo, and Linhe can all be connected this year.

Coal is the most abundant mineral, but there are no government-run mines. Commercially operated mines, such as Shigou Gou, Yingpanwan, and Gongjiban, all have very rich reserves. However, they are only sold in the province and there are no large-scale exports. If there is capital for large-scale mining, the benefits will be immeasurable.

In order to improve agriculture, the Construction Department has established a Farmers' Training Institute, which has already completed eight sessions, graduating a total of 480 people. It has also commissioned farmers to trial planting American improved wheat, Fengtian soybeans, Daixian tobacco leaves, and Guangling hemp. An agricultural product competition is held every year, and has now been held four times. Each county has formed a rural credit cooperative, with 72 cooperatives and nearly 1,000 members. In addition, the department is also vigorously promoting industrial crops.

In terms of animal husbandry, a sheep farm has been established in Wuchuan Naorenyer, where 100 Merino sheep have been purchased. Currently, there are more than 600 improved sheep and local breeds. This year, the organization of a livestock breeding farm and dozens of improved sheep farms will be expanded. Since 1932, a horse breeding competition has been held every year, expanding the horse market, sports competitions in spring and autumn, and more than 140 foreign stallions have been purchased and distributed to Wuchuan, Guyang, and other places to improve the horse breeds.

In terms of agriculture and forestry, a special agricultural and forestry experimental farm has been established in the provincial capital to promote it. Nurseries have also been established in Wuchuan, Fengzhen, and Jining to promote it widely. Afforestation is divided into memorial forests, people's self-made forests, and canal bank afforestation. Every year, about 200 trees survive. In terms of water conservancy, Suiyuan occupies the upper reaches of the Yellow River. The so-called "The Yellow River is only rich in a complete set," and the importance of water conservancy can be seen. The government-run major canals are: Yongji, Fengji, Huangtuolahei River, Yangjia River, Sha River, Yi River, Changji, Tongji, Tabu, and Gangji, each 150 li long. The Wujia River meanders for hundreds of li, with a drainage area of 300,000 hectares, which can be the largest water conservancy area. However, the project is huge and the financial resources are limited, so it cannot be completed. If millions of dollars can be invested in construction, the benefits will be immeasurable. In addition, there are no fewer than 200 canals opened by the people themselves, all suffering from economic problems and not fully completed. The Sanhu River in Baotou, the Minsheng Canal in Saxian, and the Dahei River in Guisui Satok, are each 200 li long. The water conservancy areas are all vast and the soil is fertile. However, the disadvantage is that they are not completed and the population is too small to develop, which is also a major reason. In addition to water conservancy, wells are also being dug in other counties. If they can be completed in turn, Suiyuan can be spared the worry of drought.

Southern Route Army Repeatedly Suppresses Bandits on the Fujian-Jiangxi Border Huang Renhuan Cables Victory, Recovering Guikeng 117

Shantou Correspondence: Red bandits in Jiangxi Province have gathered in the mountains on the Jiangxi-Fujian border, in counties such as Jianning, Taining, Shicheng, Gucheng, Changting, Huichang, and Ruijin, almost becoming a nest of red bandits. The red bandits in Jianning once attempted to attack Shunchang and Jiangle on the 10th, but were met and repelled by the two divisions of Fan Songfu and Sun Yuanliang, and retreated back to Jianning. At the same time, the 20th and 24th Red Divisions of the Changting red bandits attempted to attack the Eastern Route Army's front lines in Dalongyan, Daxiaochi, Xinquan, and Miaoqian from the Baisha direction, but were defeated by the two divisions of Liu Kan and Li Yannian, killing one Red Army chief of staff and one regimental commander, wiping out hundreds of bandits, and seizing more than 100 guns. The Ruixing Independent 3rd Regiment of bandits in Changting attacked the fortifications outside Wuping City and the Guangdong Army's Yan Yingyu Brigade from Guikeng Maocun Dashuikeng on the 7th and 8th of this month. After fierce fighting all day, the bandit soldiers were defeated and retreated back to Guikeng. Guikeng is located at the foot of Junmenling in Jiangxi Province, with a precipitous terrain. On the evening of the 10th, the Tahengzhong Regiment of the Yan Brigade led troops to pursue them through the night. They arrived at Guikeng on the morning of the 11th and immediately launched a fierce attack on the bandit fortifications. After several hours of fierce fighting, more than a dozen cannons were fired, destroying the bandit blockhouses and earthen forts. The bandits could not resist and retreated again. In the afternoon, Li's regiment estimated the situation in Guikeng, disarmed the bandits, killed dozens of bandits, and captured many bandit leaders. Huang Renhuan, the commander of the Fujian-Guangdong-Jiangxi border defense, telegraphed the good news, saying, "Guikeng connects to Junmenling in Jiangxi Province, and has again become a channel for the bandit army's transportation. I have ordered the Li Tahengzhong Regiment of the Second Brigade to encircle and suppress them, and on the 11th, they were recaptured. The bandits were bombarded and retreated and disarmed. It is estimated that dozens of bandits were killed in this battle, and the bandit leaders Pan Lianchang, Guo Jianfa, Liu Huanglin, and the heads of the pseudo-Soviet district government, Zeng Changfu and Liu Changni, as well as the female political commissar, Yezhumu, and 67 others, were captured alive. Seventy-two rifles were seized, and twenty-two hostages were rescued. Our army also suffered injuries: the 8th company commander, Li Dekun, and two soldiers were injured," etc. On the Xunwu front, the Guangdong Army's Huang Yanzhen Division was stationed in Chengjiangwei, and Huang Zhiwen's Division was stationed on the front line at Pangulin Pass. On the 7th and 8th, the red bandit Ye Jianying once led the most elite model regiment to attack, but they were all repelled by the Guangdong Army. Qiu Fucheng, the commander of the 22nd Regiment, was the most courageous. In the Battle of Furongzhang, he was shot through the head by a bullet and carried back to Zhongshan Hospital in Xingning for treatment. Li Yangjing set up a bandit suppression headquarters in Jipiao, on the Guangdong-Jiangxi border, and telegraphed Guangzhou to request the addition of air force assistance for the suppression. On the Shanghang Lufeng front, on the 11th, about 500 members of the pseudo-independent regiment arrived from Changting. The Guangdong Army's Chen Zhang Brigade, along with Zhong Shaokui's department in Fengrenshi, went to suppress them. They met the bandits upon arriving at Taiba, and after two hours of fierce fighting, the bandits fled in defeat, killing more than 50 bandits, seizing more than 30 guns, and capturing more than 20 bandits. The Guangdong Army has had small contacts with the bandits in the Fujian-Jiangxi border area, and each battle has been an attempt by the bandits to break through. It is heard that the two divisions of Yu Mo's department, Li and Ye, plan to move out from Xinfeng and Anyuan to attack the rear of Huichang Junmenling. (April 14)

Fujian Province Establishes Fuzhou and Quanzhou Garrison Districts Two Divisions Under the Command of the Provincial Chairman 118

Xiamen Correspondence: The Military Commission has now divided Fujian into three major regions: bandit areas, near-bandit areas, and rear non-bandit areas. In addition to the counties currently in the hands of the bandits, such as Changting, Liancheng, Qingliu, Ninghua, and Jianning, Yanping belongs to Nanping. The counties of Jian'ou, Jianyang, Jiangle, Changsha, Yongan, Guihua, Shaowu, and Guangze belong to the Northern Fujian Bandit Suppression Army's garrison. Longyan, Yongding, Xiping, Ningyang, Shanghang, and Wuping belong to the Western Fujian Bandit Suppression Army's garrison. The coastal rear areas of Minhai, Quanzhou, Xiamen, and Zhangzhou, comprising 36 counties, are divided into two garrison districts: one is the Fuzhou Garrison District, commanded by the 87th Division Commander; the other is the Quanzhou Garrison District, commanded by the 36th Division Commander, Song Xilian. The 87th Division garrisons 14 counties in the Minhai Road area, and the 36th Division garrisons 22 counties in the Quanzhou Road area and the Zhangzhou area of Tanlong Road. These two divisions have also been transferred by the Military Commission to the command of the Provincial Chairman. Currently, the 36th Division has stationed the Li Liangrong unit of the 106th Brigade in the Quanzhou and Xiamen areas, and the Fu Zhenggui unit of the 108th Brigade in the Zhangzhou area. The Fu Brigade moved from Tong'an and Anxi to Zhangzhou on the 14th and 15th. Because Song's division has a wide area to defend, it has stationed the Peng Tang, Chen Yucai, Chen Peiyu, and Lin Jing security regiments in the Xing and Quanzhou counties, and Ma Hongxing and Chen Kun in Zhangpu and Wei'an in the Zhangzhou area. The powers of the two garrison commanders are quite large. All the garrison troops, security branches, public security bureaus, and military police in the area are under their command. The following is a record of the organizational regulations of the Fuzhou and Quanzhou Garrison Commands, which were promulgated in Quanzhou on the 14th: Article 1: In order to pacify the region, suppress bandits and communists, and carry out post-disaster reconstruction in Fujian Province, the Fuzhou and Quanzhou Garrison Commands are specially established in accordance with the regulations of the Military Commission of the National Government. Article 2: The Garrison Commander is subordinate to the Military Commission of the National Government and is subject to the command and control of the Chairman of the Provincial Government. Article 3: When the Garrison Commander is concurrently held by the commander of the garrison troops, the staff of the headquarters shall be concurrently held by the original officers of the commander. Article 4: The division of the garrison areas is stipulated as follows: Fuzhou Garrison Area: Minhou, Minqing, Gutian, Pingnan, Fuqing, Changle, Yongtai, Lianjiang, Luoyuan, Ningde, Fu'an, Xiapu, Fuding, and Shouning, a total of fourteen counties. Quanzhou Garrison Area: Putian, Xianyou, Hui'an, Jinjiang, Nan'an, Tong'an, Dehua, Yongchun, Anxi, Datian, Kinmen, Siming, Hua'an, Changtai, Nanjing, Longxi, Haicheng, Zhangpu, Yunxiao, Pinghe, Dongshan, and Zhao'an, a total of twenty-two counties. Article 5: The Garrison Commander is responsible for pacifying the region, investigating and arresting reactionary traitors, eliminating bandit troubles, maintaining order and transportation, and rectifying military discipline and morals. Article 6: The Garrison Commander has the power to command the security branches, public security bureaus, military police, and garrison troops in the garrison area. Article 7: The counties in the garrison area shall be subject to the command of the Garrison Commander in matters of rural reconstruction and bandit suppression. Article 8: During martial law, the Garrison Commander shall exercise his powers in accordance with the regulations of the martial law regulations. If it is considered that the local situation requires the implementation of a certain provision of martial law, it may be submitted for approval. Article 9: The Garrison Commander shall, according to the severity of the circumstances, submit reports to the Provincial Chairman or notify the Security Department at any time regarding the handling of pacification, rural reconstruction, and post-disaster reconstruction matters. Article 10: These Regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. If there are any omissions, they shall be submitted for amendment at any time. (April 16)

The Three Provinces of Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi are Preparing to Repair the Mahua Dike The Issue of Land Allocation for Earthwork Has Not Been Resolved The Anhui Construction Department Sends Personnel to Xunyang to Discuss 119

Anqing Correspondence: The Mahua Dike, which is related to the water conservancy of seven counties in the three provinces of Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi, still has many unfinished projects after the Jiangxi-Jiangxi Engineering Bureau was abolished. Last autumn, the Anhui Construction Department repeatedly requested the National Economic Commission to allocate funds for continued repairs, which was ordered to be handled by the Jianghan Engineering Bureau, and the provinces of Jiangxi and Anhui were ordered to send personnel to handle it together. Subsequently, after the three provinces sent personnel to Wuhan to discuss the results, the project was divided proportionally by the three provinces as usual. Bidding was used for dangerous locations, which was undertaken by Hubei Province, and minor conscription was undertaken by Anhui and Jiangxi provinces. Then, the Anhui Construction Department sent Dong Xiaoshu and Li Shuqing, the supervising committee members of the first section of the Jiang dike, to rush to conscript workers together with Susong and Wangjiang counties, and jointly undertake the earthwork task of 117,000 square feet that should be undertaken with Jiangxi Province. Recently, the Construction Department approved the West Water Conservancy Bureau's telegram urging to send personnel to Xunyang to discuss the repair of the Mahua Dike. The engineering of the dike is divided into four sections. The National Economic Commission had previously assigned the entire first section, part of the second section, and the entire earth ox section to Jiangxi and Anhui provinces, and the rest to Hubei Province. However, it is not clear whether the amount of earthwork that Jiangxi and Anhui provinces should undertake according to their share, and the previous division methods agreed upon by Jiangxi and Anhui provinces, are appropriate, and how Hubei and Jiangxi provinces will carry out construction. In order to facilitate progress, the Water Conservancy Section Chief Qi Qun of the department was specially dispatched to Jiujiang to first reach an agreement with the personnel of Jiangxi Province, and to contact the Mahua Dike Engineering Office set up in Jiujiang by the Jiang-Mongolian Engineering Bureau. The Construction Department, according to the report from Wang Weicheng, the Magistrate of Wangjiang County, arrived at Fuxing Town (under Susong County) a few days ago, and Dong Li and the two committees, as well as Magistrate Li of Susong, discussed the allocation of earthwork for the dike, and held a meeting to discuss. Because the local gentry of Susong and Wang counties had different opinions and disputes were fierce, there was no good solution after half a day of discussion. The magistrates of Susong and Wang counties were also telegraphed separately yesterday, ordering them to quickly levy workers and handle the matter, and to carefully guide the local gentry concerned to work hard to assist, so that the problem of land allocation for the dike can be resolved as soon as possible. (April 18)

Jiangsu Construction Department Plans to Undertake the Jiangnan Seawall Project Selects the Best Construction Teams, with an Estimated Cost of 520,000 Yuan Appoints the Project Director, and Construction Can Begin Next Month 120

Zhenjiang Correspondence: Regarding the Jiangnan seawall project, from Changshu through Taicang, Baoshan, Chuansha, Nanhui, Fengxian, Songjiang, and Jinshan, etc., it connects with the seawall in the Pinghu County area of Zhejiang Province. It is more than 500 miles long and is the guarantee of the population's lives and property in the coastal counties. The seawalls in the territory of the four counties of Baotai Changsong, etc., are adjacent to the river and the sea, and are battered by wind and tides every day, which is especially dangerous. During the typhoon in August of the 20th year of the Republic of China, the losses were huge. In the 21st year, post-disaster reconstruction projects were launched, but due to limited funding, only part of the originally estimated project was completed. Last September, it suffered repeated risks again. Not only was the old work becoming more and more dilapidated, but also the new work in the 21st year was mostly damaged. Shen Baixian, the Director of the Jiangsu Construction Department, personally went to investigate and dispatched personnel to estimate the cost, and prepared a plan to carry out the reconstruction project, which was estimated to require 1.2 million yuan, in order to engage in construction. However, due to the empty treasury, there was no ability to raise funds, so he had to request assistance from the central government. He then received an order from the Executive Yuan, informing him that he had sent a letter to the National Economic Commission to plan and handle the matter. Shi Dejing, a member of the committee, inquired about how much the province could raise on its own. This project can be roughly divided into three types: urgent, important, and ordinary. Except for the ordinary projects that can be delayed slightly, the urgent and important parts must be carried out at present, and the cost is estimated to be more than 1,017,000 yuan. The province can only reluctantly raise 400,000 yuan, and the shortfall is requested to be subsidized by the Economic Commission. Unexpectedly, the reply from the Economic Commission last month stated that this year's construction funds have been exhausted and cannot be taken into account. However, the time is pressing, and it is really impossible to delay the implementation. The Construction Department then plans to select the best construction teams in the absence of a solution, and the scope is temporarily set at 520,000 yuan. All implementation engineering cost budgets, and the organizational regulations of the Seawall Engineering Office, as well as the regular cost budget of the Engineering Office, have been submitted to the 643rd and 646th meetings of the Provincial Government Committee for deliberation and approval. It is now actively preparing for implementation, and construction can begin around the middle of next month.

Also, it is reported that Shen Baixian, the Director of the Jiangsu Construction Department, specially appointed Peng Yumo, the Director of the Beijing-Hangzhou National Road, as the Project Director of the Jiangnan Seawall Project. His plan is to first estimate and measure the sea area and set up sectional engineering offices. Each section will have a guiding project director and several engineers. It is said that after Peng Jun was appointed, he will start to organize the engineering office and prepare to carry out the construction policy. (April 20)

Songjiang: Two Kidnapping Cases in the Large Town of South Pudong 121

Bandit alarms have been frequently heard in the various townships of this county recently. What is reported in the newspapers is almost daily. However, the usually peaceful Tinglin Town in South Pudong has now also been heard of being robbed and kidnapping people. It has been investigated that at the late Gu Yeyu's house in the Eastern Market Xiatang of Tinglin, on the midnight of the other day (18th), four or so bandits suddenly trespassed. They climbed over the fence and entered the inner room from behind the house. First, they forced the women of the Gu family to hand over the keys, robbed them of two or three hundred yuan in cash, a pair of gold bracelets, two pearl flowers, and three rings. Then, they kidnapped two nieces of the Gu family, one named Wang Jiezhen and the other named Yao Huiguan. At that time, the servant of the Gu family had already managed to sneak out and report to the Public Security Sub-bureau. The bureau only sent police officers Lu Ziyu, Wang Fengshan, Zhao Baoming, and Zhang Yingcai to rush to the scene. However, the bandits were carrying the hostages and carrying the stolen goods out of the back door and heading south. Under the light of the electric torch, it was clear at a glance that the bandits were all on foot. The victim immediately urged the police officers to chase and rescue the hostages, but they were all afraid to move forward. They instead ordered the victim to notify the security corps. Therefore, the bandits calmly escaped. Local people were extremely indignant after the incident. In such a major case, the Sub-bureau Chief Yang Meilin and the Patrol Chief Pan Xuecheng did not personally lead the police to the scene. Furthermore, the police officers who were sent were all afraid of the bandits and watched as the hostages were taken away by the bandits. Their dereliction of duty cannot be excused. Therefore, they have proceeded to jointly submit a request for their dismissal.

Wang Jinqing and Pin Yun's family in Gaojia Village, Eighteenth Ward of Fengjing, were suddenly visited by seven bandits on the night of the 17th. They broke into the gate, forbade any noise, and ransacked the house, stealing clothing, fabrics, etc., worth about four hundred yuan and escaped.

Kunshan: Another Kidnapping Case Occurs in Zhangpu Township 123

Fan Jiazeng, a farmer in Tapingtou Village, eight li away from Zhangpu Town, was a man of modest wealth and was targeted by bandits. Last night, in the middle of the night, a bandit boat arrived at the location, with seven or eight bandits on board, armed with guns, both long and short. After landing, they swarmed into Fan's house and ransacked it for an hour. Before leaving, they kidnapped Fan Jiazeng, his son A Da, and his nephew Ruzhou, took them to the boat, fired a volley of shots to show their power, and sailed towards Shuangyangtan Lake and escaped. Afterwards, Wei Renzheng, the Chief of the Public Security Sub-bureau in charge, led police and security corps members to pursue, but the bandits had already sailed far away. He immediately reported to the General Bureau and then to the County Government, and ordered a strict search for the bandits to rescue the hostages from danger.

Changshu: Notorious Bandits from Xiaoxian Captured in Changshu 124

Wang Jinming, Hao Quezi, and other notorious bandits from Xiaoxian in this province, have repeatedly committed crimes in that county and have long been sought after without success. The county government recently learned that the bandits had fled to Changshu and sent three police detectives, Zhu Wenrui, etc., with official documents to track them to Changshu and request the assistance of the county's Detective Team. On the morning of the 18th, it was learned from an informant that the bandits Wang Jinming, etc., were indeed in the Nanfang Hostel outside the South Gate. Zhu Shunqing, the Captain of the Detective Team here, immediately sent Detective Xie Desheng, leading five detectives, together with the police detectives from Xiaoxian, to go to the scene. In Room 15 of the hostel, they arrested the three bandits, Hao Quezi, Wang Jinming, and Wang Xiaofa, and brought them to the county for interrogation. Remaining News After the Fire at Zanghai Temple

Zanghai Temple in Gaofeng, West Yu Mountain, caught fire unintentionally on the 17th of this month, destroying more than ten rooms and causing huge losses. It is now learned that the number of incense burners who died in the fire that day was not just two people. On the 18th, three more bodies were found, identified as Zhang Guisheng, twelve years old, Zhang Xing, thirty-two years old, and Zhang Xiang, sixty-five years old, all of whom were temporary workers at the temple. The monks of the temple originally planned to ask the county magistrate to come for an inspection, but the families of the deceased specially went to the county to request an exemption from inspection, which was approved by the county. Cheng Genlin, Zhang Shenglin, and others who were burned have severe injuries and are still receiving treatment in the hospital. It is heard that in this fire, a jade seal given by Emperor Shunzhi of the former Qing Dynasty was also damaged and broken.

Wujiang: Villagers Kidnap Public Security Bureau Chief 125

Villagers from Chengsi Township in Xinta District of the county were staging a Huaguxi opera when Chen Chunpu, the chief of the Public Security Bureau of the district, believing the opera violated numerous prohibitions, dispatched a patrol leader and four police officers to the village to stop it. Unexpectedly, the villagers refused to comply and surrounded the police. One officer escaped to report to the bureau. Chief Chen then led two police officers, together with a platoon leader and four soldiers from the Sixth District Security Corps, to the village. The villagers, upon seeing the police, beat gongs to gather a crowd, assaulted the officers, destroyed the patrol boat, and tied up Chief Chen, taking him to Lú lú. The Sixth District Office was notified by phone and detained five villagers and one agricultural boat involved in the kidnapping of Chief Chen. They also telegraphed the county government, requesting the Public Security Bureau and the water patrol to assist in strictly apprehending the instigators for prosecution.

Long-Distance Telephone System Nationalized 126

The Construction Department of this province has issued an order stating that the city and rural telephone systems in this county, which use iron wire for communication, suffer from weak signals over long distances, making it difficult to communicate effectively. Therefore, officials have been sent to nationalize the systems for improvement. The county government submitted the matter to the district chiefs' meeting for discussion, and the following was resolved: (1) The Sujia main-line long-distance telephone system will be handled in accordance with the order (excluding the switchboard). (2) The city and rural telephone systems were originally funded by local contributions. Since the government is taking over, those funds should be returned.

Wuxi: German Anthisen Commits Suicide While Touring Wuxi 127

Anthisen, a German employee of the Zhongye Company at No. 6 Central Road, Shanghai, in his forties, arrived in Wuxi by train on the 10th of this month to enjoy the spring scenery. Dressed in a khaki-colored Western suit and carrying a large bag, he walked to the Gongyun Bridge and, standing beside the Sixth Bridge, attempted to hire a boat to tour Taihu Lake. However, Anthisen did not speak Chinese, and although he gestured and pointed, the boatmen did not understand him. Jin Pinshi, who runs the Guangming Eye Hospital near the Huinong Bridge in the city, and who was an acquaintance of Anthisen, happened to be passing by and saw Anthisen trying to hire a boat. He approached Anthisen and accompanied him to Meiyuan and Yuantouzhu for sightseeing. That evening, Anthisen asked to temporarily stay at the Yuantouzhu Taihu Villa. Jin returned to the city. For several days, Anthisen invited Jin to tour the lake and mountains, showing great enthusiasm. On the morning of the 18th, Anthisen was still sound asleep at 10 a.m. The waiter there was very surprised and knocked on the door, but received no answer. However, he could hear loud snoring. He pushed the door open and found Anthisen’s face pale and unconscious, realizing he had taken poison. He immediately reported to Wang Xinru, the owner of the villa, who rushed Anthisen to Puren Hospital in the South Gate for treatment. Dr. Li diagnosed it as poisoning, with a critical condition and little hope of survival. He is currently in Ward B, Room 2 of the hospital. A long-distance call was made to Hua Ke, the acting president of St. John's University in Shanghai, notifying Zhongye Company and reporting to the German Consulate in Shanghai, who informed Anthisen's wife to come to Wuxi to handle matters. After receiving the news, Anthisen's wife and her ten-year-old child took a train to Wuxi to inquire about his condition at Puren Hospital. In Anthisen's suitcase, they found three empty bottles of tranquilizers, a handgun, and nine bullets. The reason for Anthisen's suicide is extremely strange. It is said that he led a romantic and eccentric life and had attempted suicide twice before. Once, he shot himself in his residence with a handgun, and another time he jumped into the Huangpu River in Shanghai, but he was rescued both times.

Changzhou: Boat from Changzhou to Wuxi and Changxing Robbed in Taihu Lake 128

Lu Ronglin, the owner of a boat sailing from Changzhou, Jiangsu, to Sian Village, Changxing, Zhejiang, was transporting thirteen large pieces of cloth from Hongchang, destined for various shops in Zhejiang, and one large piece of cloth from Tongtaiheng, destined for Sian Village, Zhejiang. After loading these in Changzhou, the boat proceeded to Wuxi where it loaded additional miscellaneous goods. Setting sail from Wuxi, the boat reached Daxikou, but encountered strong winds. After waiting until the 17th, when the wind subsided slightly, the boat sailed again until it reached the vicinity of Jiaoshan in Taihu Lake. Suddenly, a fishing boat approached from the east, forcing the boat to lower its sails and stop. Nine robbers, armed with guns, knives, and sticks, jumped onto the boat, robbed it, and beat the boat owner and crew, stripping them of their clothes. They then loaded all fourteen large pieces of cloth, as well as miscellaneous goods, bedding, and clothing onto the fishing boat and left. The loss is estimated at over two thousand yuan. Afterwards, the boat returned to Wuxi and then to Changzhou, where the boat owner filed a report with the two county governments. Yesterday (the 19th), he also telegraphed the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, requesting them to order the water police to conduct strict searches and to order all patrol ships to patrol the lake one or two times daily, to quell the lake bandits and reassure merchants.

Jiangsu Construction Department Actively Preparing for Seawall Construction Project: Construction to Begin Around Mid-Next Month 135

The Jiangnan Seawall stretches from Changshu, through Taicang, Baoshan, Chuansha, Nanhui, Fengxian, Songjiang, and to Jinshan, connecting with the seawall in Pinghu County, Zhejiang, for over 500 li, providing protection for the lives and property of the coastal counties. The seawalls within the borders of Baoshan, Taicang, Changshu, and Songjiang counties, bordering the river and sea, are particularly vulnerable to wind and tides and are therefore the most dangerous. In August of the 20th year of the Republic (1931), they suffered severe damage from a major storm surge, resulting in significant losses. In the 21st year of the Republic (1932), post-disaster reconstruction work was carried out, but due to limited funds, only part of the original project was completed. In September of last year, they were repeatedly exposed to risks, and not only did the old works become more dilapidated, but the new works from the 21st year of the Republic were also largely damaged. Shen Baixian, the Director of the Construction Department, upon taking office in October of last year, recognized the importance of the seawalls and personally conducted inspections, sending personnel to survey and estimate the project, proposing a comprehensive plan for reconstruction, estimating a need of 1.2 million yuan to carry out the repairs. However, due to empty coffers, the department was unable to raise the funds and had no choice but to request assistance from the central government. The Executive Yuan then issued an order informing the department that the request had been forwarded to the National Economic Commission for planning and implementation. The Economic Commission then inquired as to how much the province could raise on its own. Considering this project, the department divided it into three categories: urgent, important, and ordinary. Except for the ordinary projects, which could be delayed, the urgent and important parts were projects that must be undertaken immediately, requiring a total of 1,017,000 yuan. The province could only manage to raise 400,000 yuan, and requested the Economic Commission to subsidize the shortfall. However, last month, the Economic Commission replied that the funds for this year's construction had already been allocated and could not be diverted. Given the urgency, delaying the project was no longer an option. Therefore, the Construction Department, finding no other way, decided to prioritize the most critical sections, limiting the scope to 520,000 yuan. The implementation plan, project cost budget, and the organizational regulations and operating budget of the Seawall Engineering Office have been successively approved by the Provincial Government Committee at its 643rd and 646th meetings. Currently, preparations are actively underway, and construction is expected to begin around the middle of next month.
