Batavia Times Editor Shen Liangmu Discusses the Crisis of Overseas Chinese: Prices of Local Products Fall, Japanese Goods Flood the Market, Overseas Chinese Merchants Go Bankrupt, and Unemployment Among Workers Increases 144

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, Shen Liangmu, the editor of the Batavia Times in the Dutch East Indies, has returned to China for inspection. After learning of this, a reporter from the Shen Shi News Agency visited him yesterday afternoon to inquire about the situation of the overseas Chinese. Shen has resided in Southeast Asia for a long time and has served as an editor at the Singapore Nanyang Siang Pau and the Chief Editor of the General News, and is familiar with the conditions in British Malaya and the Dutch East Indies. A summary of Shen's conversation is as follows:

Long History of Overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia 145

According to Shen, what the Chinese call "Southeast Asia" refers to Siam (an independent country), Annam (French colony), Burma (British colony), Borneo (divided between British and Dutch), Straits Settlements (British colony), Malaya (British colony), the East Indies (Dutch colony), and the Philippines (American colony). Most of these are islands, hence the name "Southeast Asian Archipelago." Approximately 6.5 million overseas Chinese reside there. The history of migration dates back to before the Song and Ming dynasties, with approximately 700 years of documented history. The Southeast Asian Archipelago is located in the tropics, with a climate that is summer-like year-round, and the land is fertile, yielding abundant produce. The most notable products include Siamese rice, Javanese sugar, Malayan rubber and pineapple, coconut, sago flour, potato flour, corn, tobacco, bananas, coffee, and various fruits. The most notable minerals are tin and iron in the Malay Peninsula and oil in the Dutch East Indies. The natives of the Southeast Asian Archipelago are mostly of the Malay race, with brown skin, devout Muslims, very low intelligence, and a lazy disposition, lacking the ability to save. Ten years ago, when the prices of local products were high, those who went to Southeast Asia almost always became wealthy. The Chinese are diligent, frugal, and hardworking, and are far more intelligent than the natives. At that time, Southeast Asia could truly be called "paved with gold." People from Fujian and Guangdong, after saving a small amount of travel expenses, could arrive in Southeast Asia penniless and first work as coolies. After acquiring some capital, they would become small vendors and merchants. Within a few years, they could leap to become wealthy merchants. Therefore, most of the wealthy merchants in Southeast Asia today come from humble backgrounds, and some are even illiterate.

Current Predicament: Japanese Goods Dumped on the Market 146

However, as world events shifted, since 1927, the entire world has suffered an economic recession, and all kinds of production have experienced a surplus. The prices of local products in Southeast Asia have also plummeted. For example, rubber has fallen from over 200 yuan per picul to over 20 yuan, rice has fallen from over 30 yuan per picul to over 2 yuan, sugar has fallen from over 70 yuan per picul to over 4 yuan, and other prices, such as the price of tin, have also fallen sharply, almost beyond repair. The falling prices of local products have made it difficult for the natives to make a living, and they have no surplus funds to spend. As a result, the various businesses run by overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia have been greatly affected. Countless businesses have closed down and gone bankrupt. Those who were once as wealthy as royalty are now impoverished. For example, the Chen Jiageng Company, which was once famous throughout the world, has recently closed down for liquidation. The rest can be imagined. However, while falling prices of local products are a major cause of the economic distress in Southeast Asia, another reason is the dumping of Japanese goods on the market. The Japanese have two plans for expanding their national power: the "Northern Advance Policy" and the "Southern Advance Policy." The Northern Advance Policy involves seizing our Northeastern Provinces and Inner and Outer Mongolia. The Southern Advance Policy aims to dominate Southeast Asia. After the September 18th Incident, the Japanese forcibly occupied our Northeastern Provinces and Jehol. The so-called "Northern Advance Policy" has achieved considerable success. The Japanese, having gained an inch, are also actively pursuing the Southern Advance Policy. Although the political power in the Southeast Asian Archipelago belongs to countries such as Britain, the Netherlands, France, and the United States, due to historical reasons, the economic power is largely in the hands of our overseas Chinese. The Japanese are afraid of clashing with the great powers regarding the Southern Advance Policy, so they purely adopt a policy of economic aggression. Taking advantage of the underdeveloped industries in Southeast Asia and the high prices of European and American goods, which are not suitable for the natives to purchase, they ship large quantities of Japanese goods to Southeast Asia and dump them on the market, so that almost the entire market has been occupied. Although countries such as Britain and the Netherlands are urgently seeking to resist this trend and have repeatedly increased import taxes, the Japanese merchants have the financial strength of the state as their backing, so they are ultimately unable to do anything. Even Western stores in Southeast Asia are now selling Japanese goods. He (Shen) once went to a Western store in Java to shop and saw that most of the items displayed in the store were Japanese goods. When he asked the manager why they were selling Japanese goods, the manager replied, "To make them available for the natives to buy." This shows how successful the Japanese dumping policy has been. According to those familiar with the commercial situation, Western stores that sell purely European and American goods rarely do not lose money, so they have no choice but to mix in Japanese goods to maintain their business.

Fundamental Shake-up in the Status of Chinese Merchants 147

Almost all of the Chinese merchants in Southeast Asia are "intermediaries" (i.e., they collect agricultural and mineral products from the natives and sell them to foreign firms, or transport them themselves for export, and then resell foreign industrial products to the natives, standing between the natives and foreigners, hence the term "intermediary"). If Chinese merchants do not promote the sale of Japanese goods shipped to Southeast Asia, the sales cannot be widespread. In the past, when Sino-Japanese relations deteriorated, Chinese merchants, motivated by patriotism, refused to buy or sell Japanese goods, and the Japanese suffered significant losses. After being dealt these blows, the Japanese have now devised ways to counter them. He once went to the interior of Malaya and Java to inspect the situation and found that even in remote rural areas, there are now Japanese shops. They do not rely on the Chinese and sell goods directly to the natives, and the prices they sell at are often lower than the wholesale prices offered to Chinese merchants, so the natives are happy to buy from them. The Japanese stores are always crowded with customers, with phonograph music playing. If this continues, the "intermediary" status of our overseas Chinese will be completely taken over by the Japanese. At the same time, the Japanese are also using various manipulative tactics to win the favor of the natives, inviting intelligent natives to visit Japan for sightseeing and giving them special treatment, so that they return and spread praise of the Japanese, secretly spreading seeds of rejection of Westerners and Chinese. A newspaper run by a native in Java is already publishing pro-Japanese articles, such as saying, "The Chinese come to Southeast Asia empty-handed, and when they return, they are always laden with goods, all of which belong to us natives. It would be better if the Japanese exchanged goods for our money." This shows the effectiveness of the Japanese propaganda work.

Urgent Rescue Measures: Promote Domestic Goods 148

He (Shen) has served in the newspaper industry in Southeast Asia. In his spare time, he often travels to various places to inspect carefully. He deeply feels that the current situation is a matter of life and death for the overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia. The shops and factories run by overseas Chinese have continued to close down, and the number of unemployed overseas Chinese is increasing. If they all return to China, the position of the overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia will be fundamentally shaken. Moreover, at a time when the rural economy in the country is bankrupt, if these millions of unemployed people return to the country one after another, it will only make the domestic economy more difficult. As for how to save the overseas Chinese from their predicament, this is a very big question that cannot be answered in a few words. The fundamental solution still depends on the strength of our country. But the urgent rescue measures include doing our best to promote domestic goods in Southeast Asia. For this matter, he has been speaking out in various newspapers in Southeast Asia for several years, advocating and promoting with all his efforts. At present, there has been some promotion of domestic goods in Singapore and other places, but in the vast markets of the Malayan interior and the Dutch East Indies, domestic goods are still as rare as phoenix feathers. Patriotic overseas Chinese want to buy domestic goods but cannot find them. As for the reason why domestic goods cannot develop in Southeast Asia, on the one hand, it is due to the dumping of Japanese goods, but on the other hand, it is also due to the ignorance of the Southeast Asian situation by those in the country who operate domestic goods businesses, and their failure to plan for development. If the central government can come up with an overall plan to support them, and if the state provides a strong backing for those things that people cannot do on their own, such as expanding shipping routes so that domestic goods are transported to Southeast Asia by domestic merchant ships at low freight rates, then the cost will naturally be lighter and they will be able to compete with Japanese goods. Secondly, if the central bank subsidizes merchants in the country who operate domestic goods businesses, so that they can do their best to promote sales overseas without having to worry about "capital turnover," etc. (detailed plans will be published in another article later), then people will be happy to operate in Southeast Asia, and overseas Chinese will naturally be happy to use domestic goods. The dumping of Japanese goods can also be resisted to some extent.

Overseas Chinese Yearn for the Motherland to Rescue Them 149

Although his return to China for inspection is of a personal nature, before leaving, he was earnestly entrusted by overseas Chinese from all walks of life to report the situation overseas and the difficulties currently faced by the overseas Chinese to the central government and the compatriots in the country, so that they can find ways to rescue them. Therefore, he feels that this trip is a very important responsibility. If there are any questions from compatriots in the country, he dares not fail to answer them to the best of his ability. At present, overseas Chinese are very willing to cooperate closely with the industrial and financial sectors of the country to make efforts to open up a path that will benefit both sides. In the face of the current dangerous situation, if compatriots at home and abroad do not respond to each other, not only will there be no hope for the rapid development of our country's industry and commerce, but after another 50 years, it is feared that there will be no place for overseas Chinese to stand in Southeast Asia. Now the Three Northeastern Provinces and Inner Mongolia have been occupied by the enemy. If we lose the foundation that our ancestors have laid in Southeast Asia with their blood and sweat over hundreds of years, then not only will we not be able to obtain the remittances from overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, which can make up for a portion of the trade deficit, but the surplus population in the southern provinces will also have no way to be discharged. What a dismal future it is to imagine! For the sake of reviving our nation and promoting our industry and commerce, it is hoped that compatriots in the country and government authorities will pay close attention to and assist the current situation of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia. Southeast Asia has extremely abundant and extremely cheap raw materials that can be used by our country to manufacture commodities. Southeast Asia has an extremely vast and extremely good market that can be used for the promotion of our country's manufactured goods. Please do not let this opportunity slip away. Shen said this and looked tired due to the fatigue of the journey, so the reporter took his leave. It is said that Shen will stay in Shanghai for a few days and then go to Nanjing to report to the central government.

Anti-Japanese War Wounded and Disabled Officers and Soldiers: Yesterday's Reception for the Press to Report and Accuse Zhu Qinglan's Situation 150

Hawk's Condor Plane Damaged During Performance in Jiangxi: No Major Disaster, Pilot and Passenger Safe 151

Huadong News Agency reported that American aviator Mr. Hawk, accompanied by Mr. Paley, a representative of the United Continental Aviation Corporation, was performing a flight in Nanchang with a Condor aircraft. Because his assistant forgot to lower the landing gear when the plane was landing, the plane was damaged and had to be repaired before it could be used. Mr. Paley has already returned to Shanghai. The details are as follows:

Nanchang Flight 152

Mr. Hawk made a flight in Nanchang on Tuesday. In addition to Hawk and Paley's assistant, Gus, there were also Generalissimo Chiang Kai-shek's pilot, Smith, and eight other flying instructors, all of whom were on board the aircraft. At the same time, he carried 2,800 pounds of gasoline and 1,000 pounds of bombs (without explosives) to take off and perform.

Performance Situation 153

Before the flight, Hawk gave a speech and, to demonstrate the characteristics of the aircraft, used only one pusher engine during ascent (there were originally two pusher engines). After reaching the sky, both pusher engines were used simultaneously. At the fastest flying rate, the pusher engine could rotate as many as 2,200 times per minute. During the flight, Hawk also changed the inclination of the pusher engine, suddenly slowing down during rapid driving, to demonstrate his driving technique.

Landing Damage 154

However, when the plane was landing, it was piloted by his assistant, Mr. Gus. When the plane landed, he forgot to lower the two wheels, causing the belly of the plane to hit the ground, breaking both wheels. The pusher engine was also bent and disassembled due to touching the ground. The two bomb hooks hanging 1,000 magnetic pounds of bombs were also broken. Fortunately, the fuselage was strong and did not capsize at the time, so everyone was safe. The bombs carried did not cause disaster because they had no explosives. On the same day, Hawk borrowed two Douglas pusher engines for temporary installation and flew back to Hangzhou for repairs. The damaged pusher engine has now been telegraphed to the United States for speedy transport to China for replacement. Paley returned to Shanghai on an aviation school plane the night before, and Hawk himself is scheduled to return to Shanghai today.

Fellow Townsmen from Songjiang in Shanghai Sent a Telegram to the Provincial Chairman Regarding the Dredging of the River 157

Fellow townsmen from Songjiang in Shanghai, regarding the dredging of the Songjiang River, Magistrate Jin disregards the people's strength and falsely reports wages, specially telegraphed to Chairman Chen of the Provincial Government, the text reads: "Chairman Chen, Provincial Government of Zhenjiang: In the past, all dredging of the river in our Songjiang was carried out at the end of the year and the beginning of spring, taking advantage of the agricultural slack season, dividing the city river into sections and employing farmers and workers in each county to contract for earthwork, at a price of no more than five or six cents per English square foot. This time, the dredging has been delayed for a long time and has not started. As agricultural work is about to begin, the bidding was only started. All local contractors who have always contracted have stopped. There must be other reasons. All three bidders are from other provinces. The Taichang Gravel Company, which won the bid, has no dredging experience. It has temporarily recruited thousands of workers from other provinces, all a mob of vagrants, creating an unprecedented bad precedent for dredging in the hinterland. The public is horrified. The foremen of the company are not like an army that can be controlled by military law, and the police force in the county seat is very thin, making it difficult to suppress. If an accident occurs, who will be responsible? The listed budget also sets up clever names, with the price per English square foot nominally at four cents, but in fact, additional fees are added for difficult work, long distances, and transportation, calculating the price per English square foot to be one yuan, eight cents, and four li, which is twice as much as the wages when rice was expensive in the past. The riverbed in the city river has always had a lot of rubble, so there is no so-called difficult work. The mud disposal points are all houses on both sides, so there is no need for long distances. Since long distances are required, there is no need for ships to transport. It is heard that the technical director, Xu Mojia, has had contacts with the company early on, and people are talking about it, so the inside story is conceivable. The government has clearly ordered that the dredging of the river should be based on on-site employment as a principle. Even if contracting is required, consideration should be given to rural bankruptcy, and farmers and workers should be employed during the agricultural slack season to provide relief. Migrant vagrants have higher costs for boats, food, and lodging. If each section is not properly taken care of, it is easy to cause trouble, disturbing the residents and further alienating the locals. If there are abuses such as stealing, deducting, and falsely reporting, the citizens have no way to supervise. The total amount of this river project in the old cases of the sixth and fourteenth years was only 10,000 to 20,000 yuan. This time, it is falsely wasting 60,000 yuan. Regardless of the government's financial difficulties and inability to raise funds, the citizens have no strength to bear it in this time of poverty. Moreover, local security is of utmost importance. The citizens are deeply concerned and feel obligated to speak out. In addition to separately telegraphing to the county government, we specially telegraph to the Chairman to inspect and quickly order the Magistrate of Songjiang County to take responsibility for refusing migrant workers, protect the order of the city and countryside, and, at the same time, check the budget and earthwork according to the old cases and make substantial reductions to maintain security and avoid abuses. This is a virtuous act." Songjiang Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai sincerely asks. Yun-jian Fellow Townsmen Association replies to Songjiang Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai: "To all gentlemen of the Songjiang Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai: We have received your telegram. Regarding the dredging of the city river in Songjiang County this time, your association has strongly opposed the listed budget and the recruitment of migrant workers. We deeply admire your sincerity in loving and protecting your hometown and speaking out for justice. Our association members express their deepest sympathy. In addition to writing to Magistrate Jin to adopt and implement your suggestions, we hereby reply." Gu Jiaxuan, Standing Committee Member of the Executive Committee of the Yun-jian Fellow Townsmen Association, bows.

China National Aviation Corporation Held a Board Meeting Yesterday 159

China National Aviation Corporation convened a board meeting at 5 pm yesterday. The Chinese directors Huang Jiangquan, Dai Enji, Chen Qijun, and American directors Prinn and Bender attended. Wang Xianhua, a Chinese director, has died of illness, and Picksbay, an American director, has returned to his country and has not yet come to China.) Private Aviation Participating in Joint Transportation Plans to Establish a Joint Transportation Management Office. Nine Shipping Companies Nominate Five Members to Establish an Office as Soon as Possible 165

Private shipping companies participating in aquatic product joint transportation are based on the shipping routes, warehouses, and docks owned by various shipping companies before November 1933 by the Ministry of Transportation and Communications. Those with shipping routes but no docks and warehouses are not eligible to participate in joint transportation. Therefore, only the following nine private shipping companies have been approved to participate in joint transportation: Sanbei, Zhengji, Ningshao, Dazhen, Hongan, Huxing, Daxing, Hezong, and Dada. These nine companies all have docks and warehouses and meet the requirements. Among them, Sanbei, Hongan, and Ningshao can participate in the Wuchang Road, Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Road, and Pinghan Road. Hezong and Dazhen can participate in the Longhai Road. Among the nine companies, Sanbei and Zhengji have the most ships. In addition, Huxing, Daxing, Dada, and other ships all operate on the Tongyang, Ruiping, and other ports. The participation of the nine companies in joint transportation has been approved by the Ministry. A meeting was specially convened. The result was that the joint transportation cooperative office must be established first before it can manage the dispatch of ships for transportation on various routes. It was agreed on the spot that the nine companies should first send representatives to establish a preparatory committee for private aviation joint transportation to prepare for establishment in a short period of time, and Chen Bogang, Cao Zijia, and Mr. Yang, Mr. Li, and others were publicly elected to be responsible for the preparation. Except for one committee member who will be given travel expenses, the rest are voluntary. All documents and secretaries will be temporarily staffed by personnel from the Shipping Association and given a small allowance. The preparation expenses will be shared by the nine companies and divided into three categories: A, B, and C. The fee for Grade A is 500 yuan, the fee for Grade B is 300 yuan, and the fee for Grade C is 150 yuan. The nine companies have unanimously agreed to the above-mentioned agreed methods and have notified each company to pay the preparation fee first. The five preparation members are actively proceeding.

Jardine Matheson's Dingsheng Wheel Stevedores' Slowdown Resolved 166

The stevedores of various Jardine Matheson shipping company ships demanded that the company change the year-end double salary to a three-day monthly wage increase in November last year, which led to a general strike. On November 5, both parties signed an agreement to increase the monthly wage by three days and abolish the double salary. After the dispute was resolved, all ships have been handled in accordance with the regulations, but the Dingsheng and Lisheng wheels have not been handled in accordance with the regulations, which has caused dissatisfaction among the workers on the two wheels. At 10 am yesterday, all 40 stevedores on the Beiyang class Dingsheng wheel, because the company's handling was improper, although they had repeatedly requested it to no avail, immediately went on a full slowdown to deal with it. The Shanghai branch of the Seamen's Union learned about this and, together with all the Jardine Matheson stevedores, sent cadres to mediate. The company's manager promised to handle it in accordance with the regulations. All wage increases after November 15 last year will be increased by three days per month in accordance with the signed agreement. Those before November 15 will still be handled according to the annual monthly office. The two resumed work at around 11 am.

The Tianjin Fresh Goods Brokerage Tax Disturbance Resolved. Shanghai Business Representatives Returned to Shanghai the Day Before Yesterday. A Provisional Solution Was First Set and Then Submitted to the Central Government 168

Shipments to Tianjin of Fresh Goods Will Be Notified for Loading Today

Tianjin City previously caused a disturbance by collecting fresh goods brokerage tax. The Shanghai Fruit and Local Products Association specially sent representatives Xu Yunqing, Cai Runsen, and Xu Runsheng to Tianjin for negotiations. They returned to Shanghai the day before yesterday and convened a general meeting to report on the negotiation process. The details are as follows:

Tax Collection Process: After the Tianjin Municipal Government approved the new contractor Chen Xisan to contract for the fresh goods brokerage tax, it started operations in February, setting up offices and employing more than 20 brokerage officials to intercept and inspect along the way and collect a 3% brokerage tax based on the price. They even confiscated goods for auction and detained people for fines. The format and inspection methods of the tax bills of the Finance Bureau were similar to those of the Likin, and the government did not correct them, which led to a suspension of transportation. The stalemate lasted for several months, and Japanese goods monopolized the market, affecting freight transportation from Shanghai, Guangzhou, and Ouzhou, and causing great damage. Negotiation Process: The Shanghai fresh goods business representatives were assisted by directors Huang Jinrong and Du Yuesheng, and Tianjin gentlemen Pan Zixin and Wang Wendian, Standing Committee Member of the Chamber of Commerce, and went to Tianjin for negotiations. Fortunately, they obtained the understanding of the government and signed a provisional solution with the new contractor to reduce the losses of the merchants and were allowed to revoke the order to investigate and arrest fresh goods merchants. The content stated that the goods of merchants from the South transporting to Tianjin for sale would temporarily pay a deposit, which would be saved in a bank designated by both parties, pending the Central Government's ruling on whether the brokerage tax was legal to determine whether to pay or not (excluding brokerage firms). Submitting to the Central Government: This negotiation cannot be considered over because it has not achieved the goal of cancellation. It is still necessary to appeal to the Central Government to correct the situation. The transitional measures have been signed and the public has decided to notify the merchants in each port to start business immediately to avoid losses from suspension of transportation.

20th Century Nanyang Published and Printed by the Commercial Press 171

There are more than five million Chinese living in Nanyang, with assets of 400 million yuan. Therefore, the Nanyang issue has a major relationship with the future of our nation and people's livelihood. Based on this view, Mr. Qiu Shouyu traveled extensively throughout Nanyang for nine years. Based on his observations and investigations, he wrote the book 20th Century Nanyang, with more than 200,000 words. In addition to describing in detail the natural, political, social, and economic conditions of the Dutch East Indies, the American Philippines, French Indochina, British Malaya, Burma, Borneo, and Siam, it also records in detail the Chinese population, commerce, education, immigration history, and entry regulations, etc., to clarify the truth about the activities of Chinese in Nanyang. The material is extensive, the statistics are rich, and there are more than 90 precious copperplate illustrations at the beginning of the book. It can be said to be a general collection for the study of Nanyang. The book is published and printed by the Commercial Press in a finely bound large volume.

Zhabei Public Bus Workers Went on Strike Yesterday Morning and Resumed Work in the Afternoon; Labor and Company Jointly Petitioned the Municipal Government, Presenting Six Demands for Arresting the Culprits and Guaranteeing Safety; The Mayor Promised to Strictly Punish the Soldiers Who Committed the Assault 173

Drivers and ticket sellers of the China Merchants Public Bus Company had a conflict with security team soldiers and police officers from the 3rd squadron of the police corps the night before, due to free rides. Four workers were severely injured in the beating, causing outrage among all workers. Workers on Route 4, which operates in the downtown area, announced a strike yesterday morning and petitioned Mayor Wu to severely punish the perpetrators. After representatives from the party and government agencies, along with union representatives, persuaded them, they resumed work and traffic at 3 p.m. The details of each situation are recorded as follows:

Announcement of Strike: China Merchants Public Bus Company vehicles on all routes, as usual, left the factory at 6 a.m. every day to operate. However, after the incident the night before in which soldiers beat and injured workers, all workers were unwilling to work due to lack of job security. Therefore, starting yesterday morning, they implemented a strike. After repeated persuasion by union representatives such as Fan Yifeng, Routes 1 and 3 started to leave the factory at 7 a.m., while all the workers on Route 4 drove the vehicles out of the factory gate and parked them along the Baoshan Road railway in a sequential manner. As the matter had not been resolved, the workers insisted on the strike, all wearing uniforms and sitting quietly on the buses, maintaining order.

Petition to the Municipal Government: After the Route 4 workers announced the strike, the 6th District Public Bus Union, fearing the situation would escalate, specially dispatched directors Fan Yifeng and Mao Xinhui, together with the company's general manager Huang Zhongwen, to the downtown area at 11 a.m. yesterday to petition Mayor Wu, demanding severe punishment for the perpetrators. As yesterday was the regular meeting of the Municipal Affairs Conference, Mayor Wu sent Xu Peihuang, Director of the Public Utilities Bureau, to receive them on his behalf. First, Dai Zhen reported the circumstances of the incident and presented the case for severely punishing the perpetrators. Director Xu then expressed that the municipal government would be responsible for compensating the company for its business losses and the workers for medical expenses. The municipal government would strictly investigate and punish the perpetrators, and starting immediately, one police officer would be assigned to each bus for protection, hoping that the representatives would persuade the workers to return to work. The representatives were satisfied and returned.

Strict Investigation by the Authorities: At about 1 p.m. yesterday, Fan Guoren from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Sun Jiaqian from the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, Zhu Guilin from the Social Affairs Bureau, Wen Hongen, Director of the Public Security Bureau, Wang Chengzhi, Section Chief of the Municipal Security Office, Chen Zhuomin, Commander of the 1st Regiment, and Mei Xueyan, Commander of the 3rd Battalion, drove to the entrance of the 2nd Sub-station in the 7th District on Qimei Road to investigate the truth of the incident. The injured driver, Zhu Agen, reported the circumstances of the soldiers and police officers beating and insulting him without reason, and pointed out the bloodstains on the ground. The representatives inspected the area for a week and then went straight to the Yue Min Hospital on Dixiwei Road to慰問the injured workers.

Condition of the Injuries: A reporter from Dagongshe went to Yue Min Hospital yesterday to investigate the condition of the injured workers, as follows: (1) Huang Riguang, a timekeeper, suffered a concussion and was mentally confused. His injuries were the most severe. According to the doctor, if his fever increases, his life may be in danger. (2) Zhang Shanlun, a ticket inspector, had his right thumb broken. (3) Zhu Agen, a machine operator, injured his waist and buttocks. His condition was relatively mild. (4) Wang Shuyun, a ticket seller, had relatively minor injuries.

Demanded Conditions: Based on the decision of all the workers, the union put forward seven demands to the party and government agencies: (1) Dismiss and investigate Pei, the captain of the 3rd squadron of the police. (2) Guarantee the lives of the injured (bear full responsibility for disability or death). (3) Be responsible for all medical expenses and losses. (4) Effectively guarantee that similar incidents will not happen again in the future. (5) Investigate the perpetrators. (6) The above items must be answered within five days.

Director's Persuasion: Wen Hongen, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, in order to show responsibility for punishing the perpetrators and to reassure all the workers, specially persuaded the workers in front of the company, saying, "The unfortunate incident that happened yesterday, brothers, we are jointly maintaining local治安security. You are all transportation service personnel and should value society and the country. I hope you will resume work immediately. There will never be similar incidents in the future. On the part of the Public Security Bureau, the party has ordered the police to protect the buses."

The Anti-Japanese Hero in Songhu Committed Suicide Due to Disillusionment; Wu Yunliang's Will Despised Former Superiors and Hated Warlord Mutinies and Mutual Slaughter 174

Wu Yunliang, a native of Hunan, 25 years old, used to be a sergeant in the 19th Route Army. In the Battle of Songhu against Japan, Wu had a brave spirit and always went forward in every battle. Therefore, he was shot in the chest and almost died. Fortunately, he was carefully treated at the Ye Lu Hospital inside Dananmen in Shanghai, and he was able to recover. Therefore, Wu felt that the director was like his re-created parents, and the director also valued the martyr as a close friend. They became close friends with each other. Then he went to Fujian with the army, but before long, the warlords叛變, and the historical heroics were destroyed. In great sadness, Wu left the army and came to Shanghai. Disheartened with the army, he deposited 100 yuan of savings in Ye Lu Hospital and acted as a杂务. However, the hero hated the chaos of national affairs, his ambitions were difficult to achieve, and he felt very sad. He suddenly had a short-sighted thought and wrote a绝命书the day before yesterday, sending it to Liang Baoguang, a superior officer who ran a Yuhe Shoe Store in Guangzhou. The content was purely to hate the warlords, mutual slaughter, and the urgency of foreign insults, and the country would perish one day, so he committed suicide. He had been treated kindly by Ye Lu, and he was afraid that future generations would misunderstand. Regarding the virtue of Liang and Ye Lu, he often wanted to repay them in the next life after the age of eighteen, etc. He placed the letter in front of and behind the bed and then swallowed opium and committed suicide. When the hospital discovered it, it was too late to save him and he died. He reported to the 3rd Sub-station in the 1st District, and the landlord reported to the local court. Prosecutor Liu announced the investigation and the investigator verified it. The money was taken from the deposit and Ye Lu Hospital 收斂the body, waiting for family members to claim it.

Russian adventurers Lai Weisiqi, Lao Mai Zhufu, and Baobaofu, etc., falsely claimed to be French Deputy Consul, Chief Patrol Officer of the French Police, and Head of Detective Squad, etc., conspiring with Si Dui Na Fa, La Gu Di Ya Fa, and La Di Mier, etc., defrauded the Chinese Xu Haidu and Fan Gongru of money under the pretext of allowing them to set up a gambling den, and took 3,000 yuan of ocean silver in advance. "All the bases are, I don't know English. After they wrote it, they asked me to sign it," etc. His lawyer Shen Di Gu Fu presented a license previously obtained to the court. It is a circle used for target practice and is not a roulette gambling tool. I don't know that they wanted to use it for fraud." At this point, the court ordered the witnesses Xu Haidu and Fan Gongru to be summoned for questioning. Fan did not arrive. The judge then asked another witness, the police interpreter Qian Chenglong, "You said last time that you had something to add. You can say it today." Qian said that what he wanted to add was that Lai Weisiqi said to me personally at the Deng Tuo Mo Hotel that he was Boluai, and did not mention that it was a cigarette term. The China National Cotton Fabric Market Opens Today; Implementation of a Controlled Family Cotton Fabric Industry Plan; Preparations Took Four Months and Goods Worth 200,000 Yuan Were Received 178

The China National Cotton Fabric Market in this port was organized by gentlemen, merchants, and celebrities in this port, such as Du Yuesheng, Shi Liangcai, Wang Xiaolai, Huang Renzhi, and giants of the industrial community such as Xu Mouchen, Yu Zhendong, Zhang Rongchu, and Zhang Zilian. After four months of planning, preparations are now complete, and the market is scheduled to open today. Yesterday, Zhang Rongchu, the general manager of the market, talked about the organization motive, preparation process, business plan, and future facilities of the market, as follows:

Organizational Motive 179

The organizational motive of the market is based on the fact that the number of foreign cotton纱布imported into our country every year is the largest. Foreigners also rely on unequal treaties and use strong economic power to set up factories all over the country, engaging in dumping. The cotton纱布factories run by Chinese people self相倾軋, so that the market price cannot be stabilized and domestic cotton fabrics are difficult to promote. In the suburbs of Shanghai, manual weaving is the means of livelihood. The raw materials used are mostly foreign goods. In order to挽回利权 and maintain the livelihood of weaving families, the market has this organization.

Preparation Process 180

The market was launched in November of last year. It was later decided to reorganize and expand capital on January 18 of this year. I (Zhang Jun himself) was appointed as the general manager. At that time, during the 폐历year-end, in order to调剂 the finances of weaving families, we began to收布with cash, and built a new-style market in Jiyi Lane, Tianjin Road. In February, the market was completed, the interior was also布置妥帖, the basic weaving families had 2,000 部fabric weaving machines, and contracts were signed separately. The fabric from the weaving families that has been陆续collected has reached more than 200,000 yuan, and the sales of domestic yarns have exceeded 150,000 yuan.

Business Plan 181

The business plan of the market is to专以收买various cotton fabric from各機户. In accordance with the quality of the materials organization, regulatory prices, to seven 成issue domestic yarn and three 成issue现欵, a side will be 收各goods, in accordance with the original price, wholesale to the port帮客 word number, deeply hope that各纱厂can reduce prices, in order to popularize the promotion, the revitalization of the cotton fabric business.

Future Facilities 182

The market will gradually build facilities in the future, according to the highest principle of modern social economic organization, control family cotton fabric industry, in order to achieve product improvement, quality unification, supply and demand equivalent, so that weaving households livelihood, can be in stability to求发展, social economy, on the 调剂prosperous, for a planned economic struggle, to挽　回利权also.

Municipal Council Plans to Purchase Land to Widen the Intersection of Nanjing Road and Henan Road 190

Regarding the houses at No. 160 on the southeast corner of the intersection of Nanjing Road and Henan Road, a portion collapsed on March 20th of this year. According to a report from the Chief Engineer of the Municipal Council to the Works Committee, the Chief Engineer, after the incident occurred, notified the landowner that he intended to acquire the prescribed land to widen the road and requested that the amount of compensation be submitted. However, the landowner replied that he had no intention of selling the land but had already started repairing the houses. The Chief Engineer's intention is that before the landowner carries out large-scale repairs, the Municipal Council should seize this opportunity to consider the land acquisition plan. It is found that the land in question was purchased by the late Mr. Hardoon in 1919. In 1926, the bureau planned a widening project, and the area to be acquired was 1 mu, 2 fen, and 0.8 hao. However, after acquiring this land, it is necessary to acquire No. 162, the adjacent plot, according to the plan. Only then can the traffic on Nanjing Road be greatly improved. As for the existing houses there, although the structure is not good and in disrepair, it is not to the point where the entire building should be demolished. After discussion, the committee members agreed that the land at No. 160 should be acquired according to the plan so that there would be another opportunity to acquire the land in front of No. 162 and benefit from traffic improvements. Moreover, after No. 160 is acquired, it will already have a smoothing effect on westbound vehicles. The committee then suggested that the board of directors approved it on Thursday of this week, and the responsible personnel should proceed with the purchase of the land at the corner of the road in accordance with Article 6, Paragraph A of the Land Regulations (i.e., the Yangjingbang Regulations).

Ruling Process 195

In an instant, the fire broke through the roof, and the fire illuminated the sky. When the nearby police on duty caught sight of it, they notified the fire brigades in each section of Zhabei by telephone. The fire trucks quickly drove to the scene, but the fire had already become a prairie fire. After the firefighters worked hard to extinguish the fire, it was extinguished after about an hour. Yang used his mouth to bite off a little of Cai Zhaonong's ear. After the Huishi patrol room was reported and ordered an investigation, a lawsuit was filed in the First Special District Court according to law. The court issued a summons, and Judge Zhan Liangce opened a criminal court to summon Yang. Lawyer Yan Luqing Da Yaoxian arrived in court. First, the patrol room lawyer Jiang Baoqi claimed that the patrol room filed a lawsuit for the crime of injury under Article 293 of the Criminal Law. The plaintiff rented a pavilion room from the defendant. On the evening of the 13th of this month, the defendant returned home from the outside and saw the plaintiff and his brother Cai Zhaozheng in his room, chatting and laughing with his wife. At that time, the defendant quarreled with his wife and then negotiated with the plaintiff. He went to the patrol room and was dismissed by the patrol chief and returned home. There was peace. Then, at 2:30 in the middle of the night, the defendant put on his clothes and went to the pavilion room and had a dispute with the plaintiff again. As a result, the plaintiff's ear was bitten off a little by the defendant. After reporting to the patrol room, he was sent to Renyi Hospital. He was indeed verified, and the investigation by the detectives at the house was also confirmed. That is why the lawsuit was filed. Then Cai Zhaonong voted that I am now a shorthand writer at the Economic Research Institute. I rely entirely on the sensitivity of my ears. Now that the defendant has injured me, whether there will be adverse effects in the future is still unknown. I should ask the defendant to compensate for all losses. The defendant's lawyer then claimed that the plaintiff and defendant were teachers and students. All the relatives and friends of both parties do not want to expand this unfortunate incident and are making every effort to mediate, and reconciliation is likely. It should be requested to postpone the hearing. In response to the defendant's confession, he is a professor at Jinan University. He usually stays at the school on Tuesdays, Wednesdays, and Thursdays. On the 13th, he had important matters to go home. He usually enters and exits through the front door, but he suddenly entered through the back door and his footsteps were extremely light. The servants and others were all frightened. At this point, the court held that since the two parties were teachers and students, there was considerable emotion, and the defendant's actions were also due to anger. Since there are friends and friends to mediate, reconciliation is the best. Therefore, the case was adjourned for one week and the plaintiff was ordered to go to the forensic doctor's office to examine the injuries.

Fire at Yingchang Match Factory 201

At 6:00 AM yesterday morning, after the workers at the Da Zhonghua Yingchang Match Factory in Lujiadu, Pudong, started work, the workers in the white powder room locked the door at 6:45 AM because they needed to go out for breakfast, leaving the room empty. It is unknown how, but a fire suddenly broke out. Because the white powder room is extremely flammable, there was a slight rumbling sound at first, followed by a louder sound. The staff in the factory quickly climbed onto the roof, opened the glass canopy, and poured fire extinguishing chemicals to put out the fire. Because the fire was fierce, they immediately opened the tap water and tried hard to pour water to extinguish it. However, the white powder contained phosphorus and was difficult to extinguish. After about half an hour of burning and countless water pouring, the flames were finally extinguished. There were nineteen barrels of white powder that had already been ground into powder, which were completely destroyed. The powder was prepared for the day's work, and the raw material loss made it impossible to配药, which affected all other departments, and there was no work to do. The factory immediately ordered all 800 male and female workers in the factory to stop working for one day.

Tobacco Exchange Association Sends Letter Requesting Return of Confiscated Matches 204

The Shanghai South Office of the Shanghai Tobacco Exchange Association sent a letter to Director Wang of the Suzhou-Zhejiang-Anhui Unified Tax Bureau and Director Jin of the Shanghai Inspection Station yesterday, saying, "Dear Sirs, Recently, we received a report from our member, Taiyuanchang Tobacco Exchange Store on Lima Road, that our store had batches of Shuangshou matches purchased from Suzhou Zhongnan Match Company in November of the year before last. Because sales were sluggish, there were still ten tins that had been left for a long time. This month, we received a request from Qian Xingji Store in Jiaxing Pu Ruan to pack and sell them on consignment. They were delivered to the sailing ship on the 16th. Unexpectedly, the next day we received a postal card saying that there was no market for this product and there was no need to load it, so we immediately sent someone to pick it up. When it was inspected by the inspector of the Inspection Station, it was found that only one tin had a inspection stamp, one tin had a broken wrapping, and the flower inspection stamp could not be checked. The remaining eight tins had flower stamps. The staff seized two tins and issued a receipt. It has been found that the matches have indeed been taxed, but due to the age and damage, the flower stamps have fallen off, which is not tax evasion. We hereby report to your office and ask you to clarify to the tax office and retrieve them. Our office has sent staff to the store to investigate and found that the matches were indeed stagnant in sales, and have been left for a long time, and the packaging is broken, so there is a suspicion of tax evasion. We hereby issue a special letter of certification to report the previous situation and sincerely hope that your (Bureau) Director will check and return them and avoid further discussion. We will be sincerely grateful."

L> Reading Questions and Answers <L

Reading "Tears and Laughter" 210

Reading Guidance:

I am a young man who loves to read novels, and because of my low level of education, I mostly read old novels.

After reading your "Reading Questions and Answers," I realized that the books I have been reading are completely harmful and useless. I am truly ashamed! If I were to ask myself: Why do you read novels? What have you learned from novels? I would have nothing to say.

I have now decided to follow the path you have shown me and read more new things that are relevant to my actual life. Old novels are for entertainment, they lead people to fantasize. New novels are stimulating, they guide people to delve into society. I now understand the general principle of this.

However, what remains a question in my mind is: "Why are these harmful old novels still popular for a time? Why do so many people go astray because of them? For example, "Tears and Laughter," in the current publishing industry, is still the most widely sold novel; is it because its content is rich? (Of course not.) Or is it because its technique is excellent? (Not necessarily.) According to your view, nothing in the world, even such a small thing, should be called accidental, right?

I hope you can give a correct critique of "Tears and Laughter" and similar readings. This, compared to you giving general opinions as before, will benefit readers more.

The question you have raised is exactly the question we are asking of our readers. From the discussion of general reading methods, to the specific exploration of a certain book or a certain question, this is originally a fixed procedure in our work, and we have already done so. Now, according to your opinion, let's make an investigation of "Tears and Laughter."

First, why has "Tears and Laughter" been so popular for a time? This question can never be explained by general vulgar people thinking that it is "skillful technique," or "accidental luck." We must find the root from the society from which it is produced, that is, what is its social basis? How does it cater to the tastes of the general readers?

"Tears and Laughter" is undoubtedly the work that can best express the complex and intricate Chinese society. (We cannot deny this point because of its content.) The development of Chinese society is extremely畸形. In Shanghai, we can see the towering three major companies adjacent to the quaint Red Temple, and the lightning-fast trams and cars on the same road as the one-wheeled carts. Reflected in people's minds, it becomes: those who advocate saving the country through science, at the same time advocating saving the country through chanting sutras, saving the country through Tai Chi, and those who enter and exit European dance halls, at the same time worshiping Buddha and praying to God. This kind of living style that appears at the same time but is vastly different is the social foundation of "Tears and Laughter."

Peking Chinese College Basketball Team Defeats Jiaotong Again Yesterday Excellent Performance All the Way Ahead Forty-Six to Twenty-Four Today Chinese College Plays Jinan 216

The Peking Chinese College Basketball Team defeated the Jiaotong University team again yesterday by a score of 46 to 24. The first half ended with Chinese College leading 26 to 15. The game was held at the Jiaotong University gymnasium at 4:00 PM yesterday, and the audience was very large. Zhang Wenyuan served as the referee. Chinese College's performance was better than the night before. This was Chinese College's second game in Shanghai.

Excellent Performance 217

Chinese College's performance yesterday had many highlights. Its skillful coordination and accurate shooting were far beyond Jiaotong's reach, and it deserved to be the champion of Peking. The five forwards and guards were extremely well-balanced. At the beginning of the game, Jiaotong's Bao Xin and Zhou Nu'an made two consecutive shots, giving Jiaotong a 4-0 lead. However, Chinese College did not panic. Zhang Yucai made one of his penalty shots, and Zhao Zhenji added two points, putting Chinese College ahead 5-4. From then on, Chinese College gradually gained the upper hand and developed smoothly without any setbacks, exceeding 17-6 by a huge margin of 11 points. Jiaotong tried hard to catch up, once catching up to 19-14. At the end of the first half, the score was 26-15.

Smooth Sailing 218

From the beginning of the second half, although Jiaotong's lineup was changed, it eventually fell into a state of panic due to the sharpness of Chinese College's attack. The shooting was repeatedly missed. Zhao Zhenji of Chinese College was restrained due to three fouls, but he was more careful in the game. His several accurate long shots were highly praised. Duan Zhuo also made many wonderful plays. As a result, the score continued to increase smoothly without any obstacles, 34-16, 40-20, a difference of nearly half. At this time, Chinese College's guard Wang Kanru was fouled out four times, but it had no impact on the overall situation. The final score was 46-24.

From Dai Linjing and Lin Baohua: A Discussion on the Decline of National Spirit Among Our People 227

— A Reader

This year's Far Eastern Games almost failed due to the issue of the participation of the puppet state. Fortunately, through the vigorous efforts of our country's representatives, the support of public opinion, and the fairness of the Philippine representatives, Japan's ambitions were thwarted, and the Games were able to proceed as scheduled. This is something we are very pleased about. However, during the preliminary selection process, several disappointing things were discovered. Among the most heartbreaking was the absence of soccer stars Sun Jinshun, Dai Linjing, Feng Yunyou, and others, as well as tennis star Lin Baohua.

It is said that Sun Jinshun's absence was due to the illness of his beloved wife and son. This situation is understandable. However, it is hoped that before the departure, if Mr. Sun's wife and children recover, the Physical Education Association will not adhere to the rules and regulations and will still select him.

As for Dai Linjing, everyone has long recognized him as China's best center forward. The position of center forward on the Chinese team was undoubtedly his. Unexpectedly, he lightly used the excuse that the National Goods Bank was moving as a reason to decline, saying he couldn't leave Shanghai. We believe this action demonstrates a lack of national consciousness and is a pity for Mr. Dai's glorious reputation.

Lin Baohua's absence is even more unacceptable. He actually said he couldn't bear to be separated from his beloved wife for too long, so he abandoned the great cause of winning glory for the country. This is absolutely wrong behavior, and public opinion should unite to urge and encourage him.

In short, we must realize that Chinese and Japanese are both yellow races, and their physical strength and intelligence are almost equal. The only reason why Japan is strong and China is weak is that the Japanese have a deep sense of national consciousness, while the Chinese have a weak sense of national consciousness. The Japanese are willing to sacrifice for the country, while the Chinese are only willing to sacrifice for money and women. How can we correct this weakness? However, in the end, we should also consider the athletes themselves. Life and sports are interconnected. Only under stable living conditions can they fully develop their talents and participate in sports to win glory for the country. Many athletes, because they cannot obtain stable living conditions and lack adequate assistance, have to abandon their ambitions to win glory for the country, which is a great pity. Of course, there are many people who are enthusiastic about this, and they should not be dismissed altogether. However, have our sports authorities and the general public paid attention to this point? No wonder the national spirit of athletes is declining to zero. This is a sigh in a deformed society.

Educational News

Other Locations: Ministry of Education Explains Regulations Regarding Pensions for Teachers and Staff 228

The Ministry of Education, based on a report submitted by the Jiangsu Education Department through the Wu County Magistrate regarding the case of Pan Yongyi, the principal of Yanshan Elementary School, requesting a pension, and a request for instructions, issued a special order clarifying that, upon review of the report, school teachers and staff who apply for a pension, whether they are over sixty years old and voluntarily retire, or are asked to retire by the school, or are under sixty years old but physically weak and unable to perform their duties, only need to meet the following two conditions: (1) continuous service of fifteen years or more; (2) not holding other positions. This is in accordance with the meaning of Article 2 of the Regulations on Pensions and Severance Pay for School Teachers and Staff. According to the report, Principal Pan Yongyi of Yanshan Elementary School is under sixty years old and unable to perform his duties due to physical weakness. If the principal has indeed served continuously at Yanshan Elementary School for fifteen years or more and is unable to perform his duties due to physical weakness, he may apply for a pension in accordance with Article 2 of the regulations and Article 1 of the implementing rules. You are hereby informed and instructed to notify accordingly.

Ministry of Education Stipulates Enrollment Procedures for Universities and Independent Colleges for the Academic Year 1934 230

On the 20th, the Ministry of Education issued a circular to all national universities and provincial/municipal education departments regarding the enrollment procedures for universities and independent colleges for the academic year 1934. The circular stated that the enrollment procedures for universities and independent colleges for the academic year 1933 had previously been issued for compliance. Now that the academic year 1934 is about to begin, the Ministry of Education, in consideration of national needs and teaching efficiency, reiterates the main points of the previous order and establishes detailed procedures for compliance. The enrollment procedures for the academic year 1934 are hereby stipulated as follows:

(1) All universities and independent colleges shall enroll new students by department. Students shall choose their departments themselves during the enrollment process.

(2) The colleges of arts, law, commerce, and education in universities shall be referred to as Category A colleges, while the colleges of science, agriculture, engineering, and medicine shall be referred to as Category B colleges. The departments of arts, law, commerce, and education in independent colleges shall be referred to as Category A departments, while the departments of science, agriculture, engineering, and medicine shall be referred to as Category B departments.

(3) For universities that run both Category A and Category B colleges, the average number of new students and transfer students enrolled in each department of any Category A college shall not exceed the average number of new students and transfer students enrolled in each department of any Category B college. (4) For independent colleges that run both Category A and Category B departments, the average number of new students and transfer students enrolled in each department of any Category A department shall not exceed the average number of new students and transfer students enrolled in each department of any Category B department.

(5) If universities have a "College of Arts and Sciences" or independent colleges do not have a "Department of Arts and Sciences," the departments under the College of Arts and Sciences or the Department of Arts and Sciences shall be divided into two parts according to their nature and treated as two colleges or two departments. Their enrollment ratio shall be in accordance with the provisions of (3) and (4) above.

(6) For independent colleges that only run Category A departments as described in item (2), the number of new students and transfer students enrolled in each department or specialized course shall not exceed 50.

(7) For universities and independent colleges that run both Category A and Category B departments, specialized courses shall be treated as departments when calculating enrollment ratios, and their nature shall be used to classify them as Category A or Category B colleges or departments.

(8) The qualifications for admission of new students and transfer students in schools that do not strictly follow these procedures will not be approved by the Ministry of Education.

(9) These procedures do not apply to colleges that exclusively admit female students. The enrollment ratios stipulated in items (3) and (4) may also be waived for medical colleges or medical departments.

The above regulations are intended to continue correcting the abnormal development of arts and law education and to emphasize the cultivation of more practical talents. All Category B colleges in universities and Category B departments in independent colleges should enroll qualified new students in accordance with their equipment, facilities, and campus capacity in order to achieve this goal. Unless otherwise specified in the regulations regarding the suspension of enrollment or forced closure of specific departments or programs in schools, this order is hereby issued to the relevant education departments for transmission to provincial and approved private universities and independent colleges for strict compliance. This order.

Ministry of Education Orders Sixteen National Universities and Various Provinces and Cities to Consult and Organize Summer Training Classes for Middle School Science Teachers 231

The training period will be four weeks, starting from July 15th.

On the 20th, the Ministry of Education issued a circular to various provincial and municipal education departments, stating that the statistics on the results of the middle school student examinations in 1932 showed that the scores in mathematics, physics, chemistry, and biology were the worst. The reasons may be due to unsuitable teaching materials or poor teaching methods. Teachers must first strive to enrich and improve their knowledge of the content and methods of the subjects they teach in order to improve students' levels. This work should be carried out by the schools themselves, using whatever is most convenient and appropriate to their needs. The Ministry has given careful consideration to this and has now formulated a general outline of the measures for designated public and private universities to organize summer training classes for middle school science teachers, which is hereby issued for implementation. The education departments are instructed to consult with the designated nearby universities to organize the classes, or to carefully plan for them at other appropriate schools. Once the arrangements are finalized, the departments are instructed to promptly direct the middle schools under their jurisdiction to select one to four science teachers, and to submit their names, resumes, and subject areas in detail to the department. The department should then consolidate the number of people in the province who should participate in the training, allocate them to participate in the training, and report the planning and implementation details to the Ministry at any time for evaluation. In addition to separate orders to the universities concerned, a copy of the general outline is attached for reference.

The following fourteen universities (Nanjing Central University, Nankai University, Wuhan University, Beijing Normal University, Sun Yat-sen University, Zhejiang University, Jinling University, Jiaotong University, Datong University, Xiamen University, Shandong University, Guangxi University, Sichuan University, and Hunan University) are also hereby instructed, (Beijing Tsinghua University will be instructed separately), (details omitted above). The general outline of the measures for designated public and private universities to organize summer training classes for middle school science teachers is hereby issued for implementation. The universities should organize these training classes to the greatest extent possible in order to benefit secondary education, and should select current professors with expertise and experience in secondary education, or hire additional teachers, to serve as lecturers. In addition to separate orders to the provincial and municipal education departments to consult with nearby universities to organize the classes, a copy of the general outline is attached for reference. They are instructed to report the planning and implementation details to the Ministry at any time for review.

General Outline of the Measures for Designated Public and Private Universities to Organize Summer Training Classes for Middle School Science Teachers:

1. Designated Universities: Central University, Peking University, Normal University, Tsinghua University, Nankai University, Wuhan University, Sun Yat-sen University, Zhejiang University, Jinling University, Jiaotong University, Datong University, Xiamen University, Shandong University, Guangxi University, Sichuan University, Hunan University. 2. Grouping of Training Subjects: (1) Mathematics, (2) Biology, (3) Physics, (4) Chemistry. 3. Training Period: Four weeks, from July 5th to August 15th. 4. Structure and Training Content: (1) The structure is divided into three groups: Mathematics, Physics and Chemistry, and Biology. Each group is divided into two levels: senior and junior. The senior level is for high school teachers, and the junior level is for junior high school teachers. (2) The training content should focus on: (i) New developments in each subject (approximately 25%), (ii) Research on teaching methods and teaching materials (approximately 50%), (iii) Research on experiments and equipment (approximately 25%). In addition to completing all subjects in their designated group, members may choose to study subjects from other groups. 5. Teaching and Research Discussion Time: 18 hours of teaching per week, classes from 7:00 AM to 10:00 AM every morning, and discussions on practical teaching problems from 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM and 3:00 PM to 5:00 PM in the afternoon. 6. Fees: Tuition: 10 yuan, Lecture Notes: 2 yuan, Accommodation: 2 yuan. The tuition fees will be paid by the original school, and the original school will provide subsidies for travel expenses as appropriate. The provincial and municipal educational administrative authorities or the original school will be responsible for the lecture notes, accommodation, and miscellaneous expenses. Teachers will be responsible for their own food expenses. 7. Each school will select one to four representatives from the science committee (one each for mathematics, physics, chemistry, and biology. High schools may select one each for mathematics, physics, chemistry, and biology). However, schools with 12 or more classes may send one or two additional representatives, and schools with 6 or fewer classes may send one less representative. 8. Each university will decide the maximum number of people it can accommodate based on its equipment and personnel situation. 9. After completing the training for each subject, an examination should be held, and those who pass all subjects will be given a training certificate by the school, stating the name of the subject. The aforementioned examination should include drafting implementation measures to improve science teaching in the original school. 10. Those with the aforementioned training certificate may be exempted from part or all of the secondary school teacher certification examination. 11. Science teachers who have attended the summer training should be responsible for improving science teaching in their schools.
